#+title: Ecritum Project
#+startup: overview
#+todo: TODO(t) IN-PROGRESS(i) BLOCKED(b) REVIEW(r) DONE(d) CANCELED(c)

* Project Operating Model

PROJECT.org is the source of truth for execution. PLAN.org is the source of truth
for the technical product plan until its content is migrated into ADRs and
implementation docs.

** Definition of Done

The project is done when:

- A SwiftPM consumer can add Ecritum and call a bundled scripting runtime without
  installing GraalVM, a JDK, or language runtimes.
- The public C ABI uses opaque handles, explicit ownership, explicit errors, and
  no exceptions across FFI.
- Swift, C, Java/GraalVM, Native Image, packaging, and clean-machine tests pass.
- Capability boundaries deny filesystem, network, process, environment,
  reflection, class loading, and native library loading by default.
- Permission policy is expressed as versioned objects, not informal flags:
  filesystem roots, host allowlists, loopback/network policy, command allowlists,
  env-key allowlists, and resource limits.
- Every shipped runtime has smoke tests, size measurements, startup measurements,
  and license inventory.
- Release artifacts are packaged as an XCFramework or documented equivalent,
  checksummed for SwiftPM, and validated in a clean macOS consumer app.
- Public symbols and Swift APIs are documented before stabilization.
- Accepted technical debt is tracked with owner, expiry condition, and removal
  task in DEBT.md.
- Configuration parsing, permission decisions, value conversion, capability
  lookup, error classification, and lifecycle state transitions are pure value
  transformations with table-driven tests.
- Side effects occur only in named adapters: native runtime, host callback,
  standard-library capability, clock/random, IO/network/process/env, and Swift
  executor bridge.

Every milestone is done when:

- Tasks are marked DONE with evidence.
- Required ADRs are accepted before implementation.
- Claude plan review and post-change review have been run and acted on, or the
  blocker is recorded.
- Required persona reviewers have signed off in the milestone notes.
- Verification commands and results are recorded.
- Documentation and examples are updated for user-visible behavior.
- DEBT.md is current.
- TODO/FIXME/HACK/TEMP/XXX markers introduced by the work are removed or
  ledgered.
- ABI symbol changes, license inventory, size, startup, idle RSS, first eval,
  and clean-consumer impact are checked when relevant.

Every task is done when:

- The assigned sub-agent read this task, PLAN.org, TEAM.md, and AGENTS.md.
- The sub-agent researched the relevant code/docs/tooling before planning.
- The plan includes impacted architecture, code quality impact, tests, and
  verification commands.
- Claude feedback was requested before implementation and after implementation.
- ADRs were written first for decisions that affect long-term architecture,
  public ABI, security, distribution, runtime support, or user promises.
- Implementation is complete, verified, reviewed, and recorded in this file.
- No direct filesystem, network, process, environment, clock, random, or host
  callback side effect bypasses the named adapter layer.
- Cross-boundary data uses `EcritumValue` or a documented configuration schema.

Required verification footer for completed task notes:

#+begin_src markdown
## Verification

Layers tested: Unit, Contract, Integration, Packaging, Release, None
Commands run:
- `mise exec -- just test` -> exit 0, N tests passed
New tests added:
- path/test_name
Negative paths tested:
- denied permission/error/null/lifecycle case
Size impact:
- N/A | before X MB, after Y MB, delta Z
Sanitizers:
- clean | not run: reason
Not verified:
- reason and owner/follow-up
#+end_src

** Sub-Agent Work Protocol

For each task, the engineering manager assigns:

- Task ID and exact PROJECT.org heading.
- Lead persona and reviewer personas from TEAM.md.
- Write scope and files or directories owned by the sub-agent.
- Research checklist.
- ADR requirements.
- Implementation constraints.
- Verification plan.
- Evidence expected before marking DONE.
- Relevant open DEBT.md entries owned by the lead or reviewer personas.

Sub-agents must not overwrite other agents' edits. They should coordinate through
PROJECT.org task notes and keep write scopes disjoint when working in parallel.
The engineering manager must check DEBT.md for persona-owned debt before
assignment.

Each sub-agent's final report must include the required verification footer.

** Claude Review Protocol

Claude CLI is used as an independent read-only reviewer.

- Plan consult: before implementation for non-trivial work.
- Challenge review: after a plan but before implementation when failure modes are
  meaningful.
- Diff review: after implementation.
- Second review: after fixes from the first review.

If Claude CLI is unavailable, record the blocker in the task and use persona
sub-agent review as the fallback. Do not silently skip review.

Review record format:

- Reviewer:
- Mode: plan consult, challenge, diff review, or second review.
- Input: task ID, files, diff, ADR, or plan reviewed.
- Findings:
- Changes made:
- Remaining issues:
- Engineering-manager decision:

Review loop exit rule:

- Run at least plan consult and diff review for non-trivial implementation.
- Run one second review after fixes.
- If the second review raises more issues, the engineering manager either opens
  follow-up tasks, continues the loop for blocking issues, or records why the
  issue is accepted.
- Do not run unbounded review loops without a new blocking finding.

Non-trivial means any task that changes more than one file, touches public API or
ABI, changes build/test/release/security behavior, adds a dependency, changes
runtime support, or creates a user-visible promise.

** Task State Rules

- TODO: task is defined but not actively owned.
- IN-PROGRESS: engineering manager assigned an owner, write scope, research
  checklist, review plan, and verification plan.
- BLOCKED: assignee records blocker, owner, attempted fixes, and next decision
  needed. The engineering manager resolves scope, dependency, or sequencing.
- REVIEW: assignee completed implementation, verification footer, and review
  evidence. Assignee may move a task to REVIEW, not DONE.
- DONE: only the engineering manager marks DONE after reviewing evidence,
  feedback, docs, tests, debt, and ADR requirements.
- CANCELED: engineering manager records why the task no longer serves the
  roadmap.

** Dependency and Scope Rules

- Use exact task IDs in `Depends on:` whenever possible. Use milestone-level
  dependencies only when all milestone outputs are required.
- Parallel sub-agents get disjoint write scopes. If two tasks need the same
  directory, the engineering manager assigns file-level ownership or sequences
  the tasks.
- A single sub-agent may cover multiple reviewer personas for low-risk tasks.
  Spawn separate persona agents when the risks are independent enough to justify
  parallel review.
- Research checklists are minimums. Sub-agents must extend them when local
  context shows missing sources, tests, docs, or upstream references.

** Blocker and Spike Policy

- Spikes must have a time box, success criteria, stop criteria, and artifact
  expected before implementation starts.
- When a spike fails, the engineering manager chooses one: harden an alternative,
  defer the feature, split the artifact, or cancel the task.
- A blocked task must name the decision needed and the persona accountable for
  resolving it.

** Escalation Policy

- If two or more reviewer personas challenge an engineering-manager decision
  with concrete evidence, record the dissent in the task notes.
- Run a Claude challenge review focused on the disagreement.
- The engineering manager either changes the decision, records why the risk is
  accepted, or asks the user for the project/product call.
- User-visible scope, licensing risk, security risk, and public ABI commitments
  should be escalated to the user when the evidence remains mixed.

** PLAN.org Migration Rule

PLAN.org remains the technical seed plan. PROJECT.org controls execution.
When a PLAN.org decision becomes implementation-critical, migrate it into an ADR
or a PROJECT.org task before coding against it.

** ADR Policy

Create ADRs under =docs/adr/= before implementing decisions that affect:

- Public C ABI shape or ownership.
- Swift API shape or concurrency model.
- Native Image architecture or language runtime embedding.
- Permission, sandbox, resource limit, or threat-model behavior.
- Distribution format, artifact contents, signing, or SwiftPM binary target.
- License obligations or dependency inclusion gates.
- Support claims for Clojure, JavaScript, Lua, Python, Ruby, or JVM bytecode.
- Java and host interop exposure.
- Resource limits, cancellation, teardown, and recovery behavior.
- ABI versioning and compatibility policy.
- Vulnerability response, SBOM, CVE tracking, and artifact revocation.

ADR template:

- Status.
- Context.
- Decision.
- Consequences.
- Alternatives considered.
- Verification plan.
- Reviewers.

** Security Model Baseline

Ecritum is an in-process Native Image library. It does not provide process-level
memory isolation from the host app. The security model is cooperative controls
plus defense-in-depth:

- Graal/Truffle context configuration must deny unrestricted host access,
  native access, unrestricted IO, process creation, and `allowAllAccess`.
- Ecritum standard libraries must enforce the same policy object as the C/Swift
  host API.
- Host callbacks must enforce lifetime, executor, reentrancy, queue limit, and
  error conversion rules.
- Context teardown semantics must be defined for timeout, cancellation, OOM-like
  failures, recursive stack blowup, host callback failure, and policy violation.

** Scriptability Rules

- Every `just` task does one job. Rollup tasks may call smaller independently
  runnable tasks.
- Tools that produce data should support structured output, preferably JSON.
  Diagnostics go to stderr.
- No interactive prompts in CI/script mode; use arguments, environment variables,
  or config files.
- Scripts expose `--help` with purpose, arguments, environment variables, stdout,
  stderr, exit codes, and outputs.
- Reusable scripts accept paths as parameters instead of hard-coding Ecritum
  checkout paths.
- Public ABI stability is enforced by a checked-in symbol manifest and
  `just check-abi`.
- Build artifacts are inspectable with `just inspect` or `just artifact-info`:
  symbols, linked dylibs, bundled resources, size, checksum, and runtime list.

* Roadmap

** Milestone M0: Team and Project Control Plane

Goal: create the execution system that future agents use.

Lead: Engineering Manager.
Required reviewers: Architecture, Tests, Technical Debt, Unix, Security, Claude.

Definition of done:

- TEAM.md defines personas, responsibilities, and assignment matrix.
- PROJECT.org defines roadmap, milestones, task protocol, DoD, ADR policy, and
  current task list.
- DEBT.md exists and defines the debt ledger format.
- AGENTS.md instructs future agents and sub-agents to use TEAM.md and
  PROJECT.org.
- Claude review has been run iteratively or its blocker is recorded.
- `mise exec -- just test` passes.

  phase-gate checks are explicit.

** DONE Milestone M1: Scaffolding and First Native Symbol

Goal: prove SwiftPM can call a prebuilt Native Image shared library through the C
module.

Lead: Architecture Expert.
Required reviewers: Swift DX, GraalVM Runtime, Tests, Release, Unix.

Definition of done:

- Package.swift, Sources/Ecritum, Sources/CEcritum, native/pom.xml, scripts, and
  Tests are scaffolded.
- Native Image produces private GraalVM C entry points, and the packaged runtime
  exposes the stable public =ecritum_version= ABI through the CEcritum/native
  wrapper boundary.
- XCFramework is assembled for macOS arm64.
- Swift test calls =Ecritum.version= through the C module.
- C host smoke test calls the same symbol directly.
- Minimal SwiftHost and CHost examples exist or are represented by smoke-test
  targets.
- Artifact inspection, SwiftPM checksum generation, signing/notarization plan,
  reproducibility policy, and clean-machine `dlopen + ecritum_version` smoke are
  in place before later runtime work.
- Build and test commands are represented as focused `just` tasks.
- Clean checkout setup is documented.
- CI, license, size, startup, and ABI manifest baselines exist.
- DEBT.md records or rejects all placeholder scaffolding.

*** DONE M1-004 Build XCFramework assembly path

Lead persona: Release.
Reviewer personas: Unix, Tests, Swift DX.
Depends on: M1-002, M1-003.
Write scope: scripts/, justfile, dist/, Package.swift, Sources/CEcritum/shim.c,
native/pom.xml.

Definition of done:

- `just xcframework` assembles the local artifact.
- The assembled artifact exposes public =ecritum_version= without exposing Graal
  generated headers as the public ABI.
- Verification proves Swift and C callers bind to the packaged runtime
  implementation of =ecritum_version=, not the weak pre-artifact fallback in
  =Sources/CEcritum/shim.c=.
- Packaging rewrites the raw Native Image install name to an =@rpath=-compatible
  framework install name and verifies it with =otool=.
- Script output is stable and automation-friendly.
- SwiftPM test consumes the assembled artifact.
- Artifact inspection reports symbols, linked dylibs, bundled resources, size,
  checksum, and runtime list.

Notes:

- Built =dist/local/EcritumRuntime.xcframework= as a framework-style artifact
  with public =Headers/ecritum.h= and private
  =Resources/libecritum_graal.dylib=.
- Removed the weak CEcritum fallback so the packaged runtime owns
  =ecritum_version= when the artifact is present.
- =check-xcframework.sh= verifies public/private header boundaries, public
  symbol isolation, no leaked workspace-local install paths, macOS 14.0 min
  versions, wrapper/private install names, and =dlopen + dlsym= happy and
  negative ABI paths.
- =Package.swift= and =scripts/swift-test.sh= support explicit scaffold and
  runtime modes with content-hash runtime artifact state, including scaffold
  mode that ignores release artifact environment variables.
- Claude final full-diff review on 2026-06-05: PASS, no blockers.
- Persona review round found blockers in =just test= runtime coverage, packaged
  negative ABI paths, and DEBT records; all were fixed before final verification.
- Final persona signoff: Swift DX PASS, Tests PASS, Release PASS.

*** DONE M1-005 Establish CI and release gate baselines

Lead persona: Release.
Reviewer personas: Tests, Unix, Technical Debt.
Depends on: M1-002, M1-003.
Write scope: justfile, scripts/, docs/.

Definition of done:

- Initial CI-ready `just test` path is documented.
- `just check-abi`, `just inspect`, and `just size` have baseline behavior.
- License inventory command exists even if no shipped dependencies are present.
- SBOM format is chosen: SPDX or CycloneDX.
- Unknown shipped licenses block release gates.
- Reproducibility policy is documented: byte-identical zip or rebuildable

** Milestone M2: Stable C ABI and Swift Wrapper Core

Goal: implement runtime/context/value/error/host-function foundations for one
language backend.

Lead: Architecture Expert.
Required reviewers: Clean Code, Tests, Security, Swift DX, GraalVM Runtime.

Definition of done:

- ADRs cover C ABI ownership, lifecycle, errors, threading, and async/job model.
- Runtime/context creation and destruction are implemented.
- Value and error conversion work across C, Swift, and Java.
- Host function registration has explicit lifetime ownership.
- A language-independent conformance suite exists for values, errors,
  permissions, timeouts, lifecycle, and host calls.
- Versioned permission policy objects replace informal permission flags.
- Leak and lifecycle tests pass.

*** DONE M2-001 ADR for C ABI ownership, lifecycle, and errors

Lead persona: Architecture Expert.
Reviewer personas: Clean Code, Tests, Security, Swift DX.
Write scope: docs/adr/.

Definition of done:

- Opaque handles, allocation/free rules, string ownership, and error ownership are
  specified before code.
- No exception crosses FFI.
- Verification includes C and Swift lifecycle tests.

Notes:

- Accepted ADR-002 as the source of truth for C ABI ownership, lifecycle,
  strings, and errors.
- Rejected raw opaque pointer handles for M2. New public handles are opaque
  value tokens backed by a generational registry so invalid and copied stale
  handles can be rejected before dereferencing runtime objects.
- Chose pointer-to-handle destroy/free APIs that zero caller storage, map cleanly
  to Swift `close()`/`deinit`, and return status for live-child and teardown
  failures.
- Required structured `ecritum_error_t`, redacted diagnostics by default,
  pointer+length input views, natural C struct alignment, explicit callback
  ownership, deny-by-default config parsing, and catch-all FFI error conversion.
- Required the lifecycle model to be a pure state machine plus named adapter
  effects.
- Required per-symbol ABI manifest coverage, C/Swift lifecycle tests, fake C ABI
  adapter seam, ASan/UBSan, leak smoke, and TSan before claiming thread-safe
  handle operations.
- Resolved =ECRITUM-DEBT-0002= by making ADR-002 and the checked ABI manifest
  the authority for status-code parity.
- Claude ADR review: no blockers; refinements for busy destroy, value/error
  thread-safety, stale `ecritum_call_t`, eval shape, context poisoning, and
  struct alignment were applied.
- Final persona signoff: Architecture PASS, Clean Code PASS, Tests/TDD PASS,
  Security PASS, Swift DX PASS.

*** DONE M2-001A ADR for Swift API and permission policy shape

Lead persona: Swift DX.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Security, Clean Code, Tests.
Depends on: M2-001.
Write scope: docs/adr/, README.md, PLAN.org.

Definition of done:

- ADR resolves README.md and PLAN.org examples into one canonical Swift
  permission API.
- ADR rejects informal `OptionSet` permissions for public policy and maps Swift
  ergonomics onto versioned policy objects.
- ADR defines `EcritumScript`, namespace registration, `close()`/`deinit`
  semantics, and whether `EcritumLanguage` is a closed enum or extensible type.
- README.md and PLAN.org examples are updated or explicitly marked as sketches.

Notes:

- Accepted ADR-016 as the source of truth for Swift API and permission policy
  shape.
- Replaced README.md and PLAN.org canonical examples with a versioned
  deny-by-default `EcritumPermissionPolicy`, namespace registration, and
  `EcritumScript` eval.
- Rejected public `OptionSet` permissions because they cannot encode roots,
  hosts, ports, command allowlists, env keys, diagnostics mode, schema version,
  context narrowing, resource limits, unknown-key failure, or contradictory
  states.
- Chose extensible string-backed `EcritumLanguage` with static known values.
  Unsupported or unpackaged languages must return typed errors; this does not
  claim Python/Ruby support in Core.
- Defined `EcritumScript` as a pure Swift value descriptor for M2; compiled
  script handles are deferred until ADR-003 and a C script handle exist.
- Chose namespace-based host registration as canonical. Flat
  `runtime.register("app.notify")` may become future sugar only.
- Required `close() throws`, idempotent close, best-effort `deinit`, parent
  runtime retention by contexts, and no `Sendable` claim for runtime/context
  wrappers until synchronization and TSan tests exist.
- Claude summary review: no blockers. Broader Claude plan attempts timed out and
  are recorded here as operational noise; persona review carried the detailed
  plan review.
- Final persona signoff: Swift DX PASS, Architecture PASS, Security PASS,
  Clean Code PASS, Tests/TDD PASS.

*** DONE M2-003 Implement runtime/context lifecycle

Lead persona: Architecture Expert.
Reviewer personas: GraalVM Runtime, Tests, Security.
Depends on: M2-001.
Write scope: Sources/, native/, Tests/, scripts/, docs/abi/, justfile, public
header docs.

Assignment:

- Engineering manager: Codex.
- Lead persona agent: Architecture Expert (Parfit).
- Reviewer agents: GraalVM Runtime (Banach), Tests/TDD (Gauss), Security
  (Schrodinger).
- Claude plan consult: PASS; advisory clarified that teardown failure must
  always tombstone registry state and zero caller handle storage.

Implementation plan:

- Implement runtime/context create and destroy only; defer eval, host callbacks,
  value C handles, policy parsing, cancellation, timeout, async/jobs, and
  language contexts.
- Add public ABI handles and views: `ecritum_runtime_t`, `ecritum_context_t`,
  `ecritum_error_t`, `ecritum_bytes_t`, and `ecritum_string_view_t`.
- Add lifecycle symbols: `ecritum_runtime_create`,
  `ecritum_runtime_destroy`, `ecritum_context_create`,
  `ecritum_context_destroy`, `ecritum_error_destroy`, and minimal error
  diagnostic accessors for status/category/message/operation.
- Keep the private generational handle registry in the C wrapper. Public tokens
  encode kind, slot, and generation; arbitrary, stale, destroyed, and wrong-kind
  handles return `ECRITUM_ERROR_INVALID_HANDLE` before object access.
- Runtime handles own one Graal isolate. Public callers never manage Graal
  threads; wrapper calls attach to the runtime isolate when needed and detach
  only if the call attached the thread.
- `runtime_create` creates the isolate, detaches the creation thread before
  publishing the handle, and publishes only after full success. Non-empty
  config fails closed until M2-005.
- `runtime_destroy` rejects live contexts with `ECRITUM_ERROR_CONTEXTS_ALIVE`
  and leaves the runtime valid. Otherwise it tears down the isolate; teardown
  failure returns `ECRITUM_ERROR_TEARDOWN_FAILED` and always tombstones the
  registry entry and zeros the caller handle because isolate state is unknown.
- Context handles are lifecycle placeholders under the runtime until eval lands.
  `context_create` validates the parent and increments live context count;
  `context_destroy` tombstones the context and decrements parent count.
- Swift adds final `EcritumRuntime` and `EcritumContext` wrappers with private
  C handles, an internal ABI adapter seam, no `Sendable` claim, idempotent
  `close() throws`, best-effort `deinit`, parent retention, and typed errors.
- Add C lifecycle contract and sanitizer/stress tasks with fake Graal/backend
  hooks so stale handles, wrong-kind handles, live-child destroy, teardown
  failure, optional error output, and 1,000 create/destroy cycles are
  deterministic. Include a generation-wrap regression so stale handles do not
  become valid again after a 16-bit generation saturates.

Plan feedback:

- Architecture: ADR-003/M2-007 can defer async/job semantics; basic
  deterministic lifecycle is covered by ADR-002 and ADR-016.
- GraalVM Runtime: do not extend the one-shot `ecritum_version` isolate pattern
  to runtime handles; use one isolate per runtime and call-local attach/detach.
- Tests/TDD: M2-003 owns Swift fake-adapter lifecycle tests, C lifecycle
  contracts, ASan/UBSan stress, and leak smoke; M2-006 owns reusable
  cross-language conformance beyond basic lifecycle.
- Security: block completion without registry validation, fault injection,
  manifest updates, C/Swift/Java contract tests, and leak/sanitizer evidence.

Definition of done:

- Create/destroy paths are deterministic and idempotent where specified.
- Thread attachment rules are documented.
- Leak tests or equivalent lifecycle checks run in CI-ready commands.

Completion:

- Implemented public lifecycle ABI declarations in
  `Sources/CEcritum/include/ecritum.h`.
- Implemented C wrapper lifecycle with one Graal isolate per runtime,
  generational runtime/context/error handles, live-context blocking,
  fail-closed config handling, teardown-failure tombstoning, and single-lock
  error string view accessors.
- Implemented Swift `EcritumRuntime` and `EcritumContext` owner wrappers with
  final classes, private handles, typed errors, parent retention, idempotent
  close, and best-effort deinit.
- Added Swift fake-adapter lifecycle tests, C lifecycle contract tests, C++
  header smoke, ASan/UBSan task, framework lifecycle leak smoke, ABI manifest
  entries, and XCFramework dlopen lifecycle smoke.

Review results:

- Claude split review found one blocker in error string accessors; fixed by
  validating and borrowing each view inside one mutex critical section. Claude
  re-review: PASS.
- Claude split review of core C lifecycle: PASS.
- Claude split review of Swift ownership core: PASS.
- Claude split review of generation-wrap stale-handle fix: PASS.
- Full-diff and larger Swift Claude reviews timed out; they were replaced with
  smaller focused reviews and persona review.
- Architecture persona: PASS.
- GraalVM Runtime persona: PASS.
- Tests/TDD persona: PASS.
- Security persona: PASS after adding the generation-wrap stale-handle
  regression and fail-closed slot exhaustion behavior.

Verification:

#+begin_src text
`mise exec -- just test-swift-scaffold` -> exit 0; 27 Swift tests, 3 expected artifact skips.
`mise exec -- just test-java` -> exit 0; 4 Java tests.
`mise exec -- just test-c-abi-lifecycle` -> exit 0.
`mise exec -- just test-c-abi-asan` -> exit 0; ASan/UBSan, macOS leak detection disabled in ASan.

*** DONE M2-004 Implement host function registration

Lead persona: Architecture Expert.
Reviewer personas: Clean Code, Security, Tests, Swift DX.
Depends on: M2-002, M2-003, M2-007.
Write scope: Sources/, native/, Tests/, scripts/, docs/abi/, docs/adr/,
justfile.

Assignment:

- Engineering manager: Codex.
- Lead persona agent: Architecture Expert (Euclid).
- Reviewer agents: Clean Code (Ohm), Security (Dirac), Tests/TDD (Linnaeus),
  Swift DX (Jason).

Accepted plan:

- Scope this as M2-004A: host registration lifecycle only.
- Do not claim scripts can call registered functions until eval/job dispatch,
  call accessors, and value-handle conversion are implemented.
- Add ADR-019 for namespace/function handle ownership, duplicate semantics,
  cleanup, and the registration-only boundary before implementation.
- Add `ECRITUM_ERROR_ALREADY_EXISTS = 21` for duplicate namespace/function
  registration. Do not add `NOT_FOUND` because M2-004A has no unregister-by-name
  API.
- Add public C typedefs for `ecritum_namespace_t`, `ecritum_function_t`,
  `ecritum_value_t`, `ecritum_call_t`, `ecritum_host_fn_t`, and
  `ecritum_user_data_destroy_fn_t`.
- Add public C APIs for namespace create/destroy, namespace function
  registration, and function destroy.
- Store namespace/function records in the existing generational registry and
  under the owning runtime. Names are copied and validated before ownership
  transfer.
- User data transfers only after successful registration. Failed registration
  never calls `destroy_user_data`; successful registration cleanup runs exactly
  once through function destroy, namespace destroy, or runtime destroy.
- Destructors and future callbacks must never run while registry/runtime/
  context/job/function locks are held.
- Swift adds `EcritumNamespace`, `EcritumNamespace.Name`,
  `EcritumFunctionName`, `EcritumHostFunction`, and an `EcritumCall` shell with
  no public raw-handle exposure.
- Swift callbacks run directly on the future Ecritum worker thread by default;
  no implicit `MainActor` hop.
- Callback success/error is tested through Swift fake adapters and
  `ECRITUM_TESTING` C hooks only.

Plan review:

- Claude ADR-019 review: PASS; non-blocking name-length cap added.
- Architecture persona: PASS.
- Clean Code persona: PASS.
- Security persona: PASS.
- Tests/TDD persona: PASS.
- Swift DX persona: PASS.

Implementation notes:

- Added ADR-019 as the accepted host-registration lifecycle decision record.
- Added public C ABI typedefs and entrypoints for namespaces, functions,
  callback typedefs, reserved value/call handles, and duplicate status
  `ECRITUM_ERROR_ALREADY_EXISTS = 21`.
- Implemented namespace/function records in the existing generational C registry
  with copied validated names, per-runtime isolation, stale/wrong-kind handle
  rejection, and destructor cleanup outside the registry lock.
- Runtime destroy now refuses live contexts as before, then tombstones and
  cleans owned namespaces/functions before Native Image isolate teardown.
- Added Swift registration wrappers: `EcritumRuntime.namespace`,
  `EcritumNamespace`, `EcritumNamespace.Name`, `EcritumFunctionName`,
  `EcritumHostFunction`, and an internal-handle `EcritumCall` shell.
- Added C and Swift contract tests for name validation, duplicates, failed
  registration ownership, namespace/function/runtime cleanup, stale handles,
  runtime isolation, callback success, and callback failure.
- Updated Java/Swift/C status tables, ABI manifest, C++ header smoke, just
  tasks, and XCFramework `dlopen` smoke coverage for the new public symbols.
- Fixed post-review issues: Swift namespace close after runtime cascade is a
  no-op, duplicate namespace is covered in C, Swift fake runtime ownership is
  runtime-scoped, `function_destroy` uses a single cleanup slot, and the real
  Swift C-adapter failed-registration path now has weak-reference release
  coverage.
- Added the security reviewer follow-up regression instead of ledgering debt:
  runtime destroy with a live context leaves registered functions alive and only
  runs destructors after the context is closed and runtime destroy succeeds.

*** DONE M2-005 Implement policy/config parsing core

Lead persona: Security.
Reviewer personas: Clean Code, Tests, Architecture, Swift DX.

Initial scope decision:

- Do not block M2-005 on ADR-004. ADR-004 remains the M2.5 enforcement and
  untrusted-script threat-model ADR; M2-005 owns parsing, validation,
  deterministic serialization, and storing policy/config as data only.
- Added proposed ADR-020 for the narrower config schema because M2-005 fixes a
  cross-language schema consumed by the public C create APIs and Swift wrapper.
- Split M2-005 into M2-005A if needed: pure policy/config data model,
  deterministic Swift serialization, C schema parser/validator, and runtime
  vs context narrowing checks. Do not implement filesystem/network/process/env
  access or runtime enforcement yet.
- Keep runtime policy as the maximum grant. Context configuration may only
  narrow. Widening fails before context creation with
  `ECRITUM_ERROR_INVALID_CONFIG` in M2-005.
- Preserve safe defaults: empty runtime config and Swift runtime `.default` mean
  schema v1 defaults with denied capabilities and no raw GraalVM passthrough
  options; empty context config means no additional narrowing and inherits the
  parent runtime effective config.
- Implement tests before production code per TDD. Red tests must cover default
  deny, explicit narrow allowlists, unknown key/version failure, invalid JSON/
  UTF-8, deterministic canonical JSON, C parser rejection, and context widening.

*** DONE M2-006 Create shared conformance suite

Lead persona: Tests.
Reviewer personas: Clean Code, Security, Unix.
Depends on: M2-002, M2-005.
Write scope: Tests/, scripts/, justfile, .gitignore.

Assignment:

- Engineering manager: Codex.
- Lead persona agent: Tests/TDD (Ada).
- Reviewer agents: Clean Code (Beck), Security (Fermat), Unix tooling (Ken).
- Architecture consult: requested from Architecture Expert (Dewey) because the
  provider protocol has architectural weight; proceed only with an internal,
  reversible test-harness contract unless that review requires an ADR.
- Claude plan consult: PASS. Claude agreed M2-006 should build the authoritative
  manifest, runner, and fixture provider protocol now because no eval/job ABI
  exists yet; real language providers must plug into the same manifest later.

Accepted plan:

- Create a data-driven `Tests/Conformance/` suite that enumerates every required
  Cross-Language Conformance Suite case.
- Add `scripts/run-conformance.py` as the runner. It owns manifest parsing,
  provider invocation, result normalization, deterministic JSON stdout,
  diagnostics on stderr, and CI-friendly exit codes.
- Keep the provider protocol internal to the test harness for M2-006. It is not
  public ABI, not a language-support promise, and can change before real
  providers land.
- Add fixture providers/tests that prove pass, fail, pending capability,
  malformed provider output, provider crash, provider timeout, filtering, and
  stable summary behavior.
- Make unsupported eval, timeout, script-host-call, and script-permission cases
  explicit pending capability evidence until the eval/job/provider ABI exists.
  Pending required cases must prevent any language from being reported
  conformant.
- Reuse existing C and Swift checks for lifecycle, host-registration,
  policy/config, value, error, and allocation/release evidence instead of
  duplicating their implementation in the runner.

Scope guardrails:

- Do not implement real language adapters in M2-006.
- Do not claim Clojure, JavaScript, Python, Ruby, Lua, or JVM conformance from
  fixture-provider results.
- Do not define public C ABI, Swift API, sandbox enforcement semantics, or
  filesystem canonicalization behavior in the runner. If implementation needs
  those decisions, stop and write an ADR first.
- Default-deny permission cases must include filesystem, network, process,
  environment, reflection, class loading, native library loading, and
  unrestricted Java lookup.

Pre-implementation review:

- Tests/TDD: PASS. Red tests must cover required-case catalog completeness,
  explicit pending capability behavior, provider capability mismatch, conformant
  summary false with pending required cases, and current C/Swift evidence.
- Clean Code: PASS with guardrail. Keep manifest validation pure/table-driven,
  provider invocation in a thin side-effect boundary, and no framework
  dependency.
- Security: PASS with guardrail. False-green output is the main risk; denied
  cases must be visible pending/failing evidence, not silent skips.
- Unix tooling: PASS. Runner must use deterministic JSON stdout, stderr-only
  diagnostics, `--list`, filters, and distinct exit codes.
- Architecture: PASS. No ADR is required while the protocol stays test-internal
  under `Tests/`, `scripts/`, and `justfile`, mirrors ADR-002/003/014/020, and
  does not define new public value/error/timeout/policy semantics. ADR required
  if the provider JSON becomes stable, shipped, third-party-facing, or a support
  contract.

Internal protocol details:

- Manifest fields: `schemaVersion`, `suite`, `cases`; each case has `caseId`,
  `title`, `category`, `required`, `capabilities`, `description`, optional
  `request`, and optional `expected`.
- Provider stdin: one JSON object with `protocolVersion`, `provider`, and the
  selected `cases`.
- Provider stdout: one JSON object with `protocolVersion`, `provider.id`,
  `provider.capabilities`, and `results`.
- Provider result fields: `caseId`, `status` (`pass`, `fail`,
  `pending_capability`, or `error`), `reason`, optional `evidence`, and optional
  normalized `actual`.
- Runner exit codes: `0` for harness success, `1` for required failures or
  strict-mode pending required cases, and `2` for runner/provider protocol
  errors.
- Pending required cases are allowed in normal harness validation only when the
  provider lacks the case capabilities and gives a non-empty reason. They must
  set the provider summary `conformant` value to false. Strict mode is the
  support-claim gate and fails on pending required cases.

Verification plan:

- Red: `mise exec -- just conformance` fails before the just task/runner exists.
- Red: `python3 -m unittest Tests/Conformance/test_runner.py` fails before the
  runner and manifest exist.
- Green: `python3 -m py_compile scripts/run-conformance.py`.
- Green: `python3 -m unittest Tests/Conformance/test_runner.py`.
- Green: `mise exec -- just conformance`.
- Green: `mise exec -- just test-swift-scaffold`.
- Green: `mise exec -- just test-c-abi-lifecycle`.
- Green: `mise exec -- just test-c-abi-host-registration`.
- Green: `mise exec -- just test-c-abi-policy-config`.
- Green: `mise exec -- just test`.
- Review: Claude diff review, then persona review; run one second Claude review
  if fixes are required.

Definition of done:

- Suite implements the authoritative cases listed in the Cross-Language
  Conformance Suite section.
- Suite can run against each language provider through the same contract.
- Output is scriptable and CI-friendly.
- Required pending cases are visible and make the provider/language summary
  non-conformant until real runtime support exists.

Post-change review completed:

- Security review: PASS. Default-deny catalog, false-pass guards,
  strict/pending gate, fixture-only boundary, and just integration had no
  blockers.
- Clean Code review: PASS. Manifest validation and provider side effects are
  separated, and fixture I/O is contained.
- Tests/TDD review: BLOCKER then PASS. Initial review found that a provider
  could declare `eval`, return a bare `pass`, and become conformant without
  proving expected output. Fixed by validating pass results against manifest
  `expected` values/evidence and adding regression tests.
- Unix tooling review: BLOCKER then PASS. Initial review found provider stderr
  was embedded in JSON stdout and help did not document streams/exit codes.
  Fixed by forwarding provider stderr to stderr only and documenting runner
  streams and exit codes.
- Claude diff review: found false-green/test-gap risks around all-pass fixture
  mode, pass-without-capability coverage, expected-output validation, stderr
  handling, and CLI edge cases.
- Claude second review: PASS. Confirmed all prior blockers were resolved and no
  new issues were introduced.

Red/green evidence:

- Red: `mise exec -- just conformance` failed before implementation because
  `justfile` did not contain recipe `conformance`.
- Red: `python3 -m unittest Tests/Conformance/test_runner.py` failed before
  implementation because `Tests/Conformance/manifest.json` and
  `scripts/run-conformance.py` did not exist.
- Red after review: expanded regression tests failed on `all-pass` fixture mode,
  missing help text, bare pass without expected `actual`, wrong expected
  `actual`, and provider stderr in JSON stdout.
- Green: runner now validates manifest coverage, provider protocol shape,
  pass-without-capability, pass-vs-expected actual/evidence, pending
  capability reasons, strict pending gates, malformed output, provider crash,
  provider timeout, filtering, listing, unknown cases, empty selections, and
  stderr/stdout separation.

*** DONE M2-007 ADR for async, cancellation, and teardown

Lead persona: Architecture Expert.
Reviewer personas: Security, Tests, Swift DX, GraalVM Runtime.
Depends on: M2-001.
Write scope: docs/adr/.

Assignment:

- Engineering manager: Codex.
- Lead persona agent: Architecture Expert (Dewey).
- Reviewer agents: Security (Fermat), Tests/TDD (Ramanujan), Swift DX
  (Lagrange), GraalVM Runtime (Archimedes).
- Claude plan consult: timed out on a bounded no-tools prompt; do not count as
  review evidence. Proceeding from persona reviews and focused post-draft
  Claude review.

Accepted plan:

- Split M2-007 into the two PROJECT-tracked ADR outputs:
  - ADR-003: runtime/context concurrency and async job model.
  - ADR-014: resource limits, cancellation, teardown, and recovery.
- Define `ecritum_job_t` as an owned generational handle scoped under a context.
- Make async eval primary; synchronous eval is sugar over start, wait, result,
  and destroy.
- Keep one active job per context in M2; overlapping context work returns
  `ECRITUM_ERROR_BUSY`.
- Distinguish execution timeout from wait timeout. Execution timeout is
  terminal `ECRITUM_ERROR_TIMEOUT`; wait timeout is normal observation and
  returns `ECRITUM_OK` with a nonterminal job state.
- Keep cancellation cooperative and best-effort until per-language backend tests
  prove stronger behavior. Do not claim preemptive thread kill or hard
  interruption for hostile in-process code.
- Poison the context after timeout/cancellation unless the backend proves reuse
  is safe for that language. Runtime safety failures require runtime poisoning
  or teardown.
- Forbid same-runtime blocking reentry from callbacks in M2. Callback execution
  must never run while registry/context/job locks are held.
- Keep Swift public API as `async throws` and hide C job handles behind the
  wrapper initially. Runtime/context/job/call wrappers remain non-`Sendable`
  until synchronization and TSan coverage exist.

Definition of done:

- ADR defines job handles, timeout behavior, cancellation, teardown after
  failure, callback reentrancy, executor hopping, and deadlock prevention.
- Verification plan includes recursion, large allocation, timeout,
  cancellation, and callback failure tests.

Completion:

- Added `docs/adr/0003-runtime-context-concurrency-and-async-job-model.md`.
- Added `docs/adr/0014-resource-limits-cancellation-teardown-and-recovery.md`.
- ADR-003 defines the owned `ecritum_job_t` handle, job states, async eval
  API, worker-thread execution model, GraalVM attach/detach rules, wait timeout
  semantics, cancellation state, callback reentrancy, lock order, Swift async
  mapping, and verification requirements.
- ADR-014 defines monotonic deadlines, cooperative cancellation, resource-limit
  narrowing, conservative context poisoning, teardown rules, GraalVM/backend
  boundaries, callback recovery, Swift recoverability mapping, and verification
  requirements.

Review results:

- Claude plan consult: timed out and was not counted as evidence.
- Claude ADR-003 review: found blockers in execution thread model, GraalVM
  attach/detach rules, overloaded wait timeout status, cancellation transition,
  and async input ownership. Fixed all blockers.
- Claude ADR-003 re-review: PASS; minor pending-cancel clarification fixed.
- Claude ADR-014 full review: timed out. Split reviews for deadline/recovery and
  teardown/callback halves: PASS. Minor `UINT64_MAX` wait-sentinel ambiguity
  fixed by reserving it as invalid for M2.
- Architecture persona: PASS.
- Security persona: PASS.
- Tests/TDD persona: PASS.
- Swift DX persona: PASS.
- GraalVM Runtime persona: PASS.

Verification:

#+begin_src text
`mise exec -- just plan-check` -> exit 0.
ADR-003 covers job handles, timeout behavior, callback reentrancy, executor hopping, and deadlock prevention.
ADR-014 covers cancellation, teardown after failure, resource limits, poisoned recovery, recursion/large allocation/timeout/cancellation/callback failure verification.

** Milestone M2.5: Sandbox Hardening Gate

Goal: define and test the security boundary before exposing Clojure to users.

Lead: Security.
Required reviewers: Architecture, Tests, GraalVM Runtime, Clean Code.

Definition of done:

- ADR covers sandbox enforcement architecture and in-process limitations.
- Forbidden Polyglot settings are rejected by tests or static checks.
- C ABI functions handle nulls, invalid handles, use-after-destroy,
  double-destroy, oversized inputs, and concurrent calls safely.
- Fuzz targets or equivalent parser abuse tests exist for C ABI/value/config
  parsing.
- Threat model and vulnerability-response tasks are recorded.

Post-change review completed:

*** DONE M3-001 ADR for SCI and Babashka compatibility scope

Lead persona: GraalVM Runtime.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Security, Tests, Release.
Write scope: docs/adr/.

Definition of done:

- Supported namespaces and non-goals are explicit.
- Arbitrary classpath and Maven loading are rejected for v0.
- Verification plan includes native-image smoke tests.

Assignment:

- Engineering manager: Codex.
- Lead persona agent: GraalVM Runtime.
- Reviewer agents: Architecture, Security, Tests/TDD, Release.
- Claude plan consult: read-only consult timed out after 240 seconds with no
  output; do not count it as review evidence. Persona reviewers used Claude
  where practical and recorded their results.

Accepted plan:

- Write ADR-005 as the gate for M3-002, not as an implementation.
- Embed SCI directly. Do not shell out to `bb` and do not expose a Babashka task
  runner, pods, dynamic dependency loading, or arbitrary project loading.
- Scope Clojure support as Babashka-like only for explicitly listed namespaces
  and behavior. Do not claim full Babashka compatibility.
- Keep the public ABI language-neutral and tied to ADR-003 async eval/job
  handles plus generic Ecritum value/call accessors. No Clojure-specific,
  JVM-specific, or C++ public surface.
- Deny raw Java interop, class lookup, `new`, static calls, reflection,
  classpath/JAR/Maven/add-deps mutation, `load-file`, unrestricted
  `clojure.java.io`, raw `babashka.fs`, raw `babashka.process`, and caller-
  supplied SCI options.
- Project host functions as Clojure vars only through explicit registered
  Ecritum namespaces, converting arguments/results through `EcritumValue` and
  preserving ADR-003/014 callback rules.
- Require exact dependency pins, shipped/build/test license inventory, EPL
  obligations, Native Image metadata audit, size/startup/RSS/first-eval gates,
  `license-report`/`check-dep-delta`, and clean-machine proof with no GraalVM,
  JDK, Clojure, `bb`, or classpath dependency installed.
- Verification must include Native Image Clojure eval smoke, Swift
  XCFramework smoke, strict Clojure conformance provider, namespace matrix,
  Clojure escape-hatch denial tests, source/error diagnostics, timeout/cancel
  behavior, `test-security-*`, `just size`, `bench-*`, license gates, and no
  Clojure support claim until strict conformance has zero required pending
  cases.

Pre-implementation review:

- GraalVM Runtime: PASS plan with mandatory exact dependency pins, embedded SCI,
  curated namespaces, host projection, security-denial, Native Image, strict
  conformance, perf, and release gates. Claude timed out in the persona review.
- Architecture: BLOCKER until ADR-005 requires ADR-003 async eval/job ABI,
  generic value/call accessors, exact host-function projection, no
  Clojure-specific or JVM/C++ public surface, and strict conformance.
- Security: BLOCKER until ADR-005 explicitly denies SCI Java interop,
  classpath/Maven/add-deps/loading, pods, raw process/fs/network/env, caller-
  supplied SCI opts, and untrusted-code claims for CE in-process artifacts.
- Tests/TDD: BLOCKER until ADR-005 requires Native Image eval smoke, Swift
  smoke, strict Clojure conformance, escape-hatch denials, namespace matrix,
  source/error diagnostics, timeout/cancel tests, and ADR-018 perf gates.
- Release: BLOCKER until ADR-005 requires exact pins, shipped vs build/test
  SPDX/license inventory, EPL obligations, resource packaging rules,
  clean-machine proof, and `license-report`/`check-dep-delta` updates.

Implementation:

- Added `docs/adr/0005-sci-babashka-compatibility-scope.md`.
- Accepted embedded SCI as the M3 Clojure evaluator and explicitly rejected
  shelling out to `bb`, full Babashka compatibility, dynamic dependencies,
  pods, arbitrary project loading, and arbitrary JVM Clojure.
- Kept Clojure on the language-neutral ADR-003 eval/job path with generic
  Ecritum values, calls, and structured errors.
- Defined the supported namespace set, deferred/wrapped namespaces, denied SCI
  and Java escape hatches, host-function projection, diagnostics, timeout/
  cancellation recovery, dependency/license gates, Native Image metadata policy,

- Marked ADR-005 accepted in the ADR backlog.

Verification:

*** DONE M3-002 Implement Clojure eval and host calls

Lead persona: GraalVM Runtime.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Clean Code, Tests, Security, Release.
Depends on: M3-001, M2-006, M2.5-002.
Write scope: native/, Sources/, Tests/.

Definition of done:

- Eval scalar/object/array smoke tests pass from Swift.
- Script-to-host and host-return-to-script tests pass.
- Language errors include source names and useful stack data.

Assignment:

- Engineering manager: Codex.
- Lead persona agent: GraalVM Runtime.
- Reviewer agents: Architecture, Clean Code, Tests/TDD, Security, Release.
- Claude plan consult: required before implementation; call `claude -p`
  directly without an auth check.

Research notes:

- Local source has C value handle typedefs but no public value constructors,
  accessors, or destroy function yet.
- ADR-003 requires `ecritum_job_t`, `ecritum_eval_start`, finite wait/poll,
  single-drain `job_result`, and busy context semantics.
- Swift has `EcritumValue`, lifecycle wrappers, namespace registration, and
  host callback registration, but no async eval API and the current C callback
  bridge discards returned values.
- Clojars checked on 2026-06-05: `org.babashka/sci` current version is
  `0.12.51`, EPL-1.0, with transitive dependencies `borkdude/edamame`
  `1.5.37`, `borkdude/graal.locking` `0.0.2`,
  `org.babashka/sci.impl.types` `0.0.2`, and `org.clojure/clojure`
  `1.10.3`.

Accepted implementation split:

- M3-002A adds the language-neutral eval/job/value ABI, C contract tests, and
  Swift async eval wrapper over the job state machine.
- M3-002B embeds SCI with the exact dependency pin, scalar/array/object value
  conversion, source-name diagnostics, and Native Image smoke tests.
- M3-002C projects registered host functions into SCI namespaces, propagates
  callback return values/errors, and wires strict Clojure conformance/security
  provider cases.
- M3-002 remains incomplete until all three slices are complete, reviewed, and
  verified.

Roll-up status:

- 2026-06-05: M3-002A, M3-002B, and M3-002C are all done and verified.
- Parent DoD evidence: Swift artifact-backed eval returns scalar/array/object
  values; script-to-host and host-return-to-script tests pass from C, Swift,
  Native Image, XCFramework, and strict packaged Clojure conformance; language
  errors include structured operation/language/source-name/category/message
  diagnostics.
- Structured script stack-frame accessors are not part of the current public C
  ABI and are tracked as `ECRITUM-DEBT-0007` for the M4.5 ABI diagnostic review.
- Claude plan/post-change reviews for the latest M3-002C slice timed out and
  are not counted as signoff. Persona reviews and the `test-m3-002c` gate are
  the accepted completion evidence.

Pre-implementation plan for M3-002A:

- Red tests first: C job lifecycle and value accessor contract tests, Swift
  async eval wrapper tests using a fake ABI, and callback result propagation
  tests.
- Keep the public ABI language-neutral: `ecritum_job_t`, `ecritum_eval_start`,
  job state constants, value constructors/accessors/destroy, call argument
  accessors, and no Clojure-specific symbol.
- Implement the smallest test-mode backend that can drive the new ABI while
  preserving ADR-003 single-job busy and single-drain result semantics.
- Production SCI work waits for M3-002B after M3-002A's public surface is
  reviewed and stable enough for the Native Image adapter.

Verification plan for M3-002A:

- `mise exec -- just test-c-abi-eval`
- `mise exec -- just test-c-abi-eval-asan`
- `mise exec -- just check-abi`
- `mise exec -- just test-swift-scaffold`
- `mise exec -- just conformance`
- `mise exec -- just test`

**** DONE M3-002A Add language-neutral eval/job/value ABI and Swift async wrapper

Lead persona: GraalVM Runtime.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Clean Code, Tests/TDD, Security.
Write scope: Sources/CEcritum/include/ecritum.h, Sources/Ecritum/, Tests/C/,
Tests/EcritumTests/, scripts/ecritum_runtime_wrapper.c, justfile.

Definition of done:

- ADR-021 is accepted before public value/call accessor implementation lands.
- Public C ABI exposes documented job and value functions without
  Clojure-specific symbols.
- C contract tests prove eval start, poll/wait/result/destroy, busy context,
  cancel idempotence, `UINT64_MAX` wait rejection, active destroy rejection,
  single-drain result/error ownership, undrained-result destroy, invalid/stale/
  wrong-kind handles, and value accessors.
- Swift async eval wrapper tests pass through a fake ABI and preserve
  `EcritumValue` kinds, finite wait/result/destroy order, timeout/cancel
  mapping, native cancel on Swift task cancellation, and no public job handle.
- Callback return values are no longer discarded by the Swift/C bridge;
  callback argument access, active-call cleanup pinning, callback result/error
  precedence, and returned-value cleanup are tested.
- `docs/abi/ecritum-c-abi.json`, `Tests/C/header_cpp_smoke.cpp`, and
  conformance allocation/release evidence include the new symbols and tests.
- The M3-002A fake evaluator is compiled only under `ECRITUM_TESTING` and does
  not false-green real Clojure eval, host, timeout, or permission conformance.

Completion evidence:

- ADR-021 accepted before implementation.
- Implemented public value/call/eval/job ABI in `ecritum.h`, the native wrapper,
  Swift async eval wrappers, and Swift `EcritumCall.argumentCount()` /
  `EcritumCall.value(at:)`.
- C contract coverage includes value accessors, job lifecycle, single-drain
  result ownership, active destroy pinning, stale/wrong-kind/arbitrary handles,
  invalid callback result handles, same-runtime callback reentry rejection,
  callback-scope invalidation, empty object-key duplicates, and registry
  exhaustion under ASan/UBSan.

  callback argument access through a fake adapter, artifact invalid-call access,
  and artifact-backed partial native value construction cleanup.
- Verification passed:
  `mise exec -- just test-c-abi-eval`;
  `mise exec -- just test-c-abi-eval-asan`;
  `mise exec -- just test-swift-scaffold`;
  `mise exec -- just test-swift-auto`;

  `mise exec -- just xcframework`;
  `mise exec -- just test`.
- Review evidence: Architecture PASS; Clean Code PASS; Tests/TDD PASS;
  Security PASS; Swift DX PASS; Unix/reusable-components PASS.
- Claude review evidence: initial broad review found the missing
  `EcritumCall.value(at:)` blocker; final micro-review returned PASS for the

**** DONE M3-002B Embed SCI eval backend

Lead persona: GraalVM Runtime.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Clean Code, Tests/TDD, Security, Release.
Write scope: native/, Tests/, scripts/, justfile, docs/release-gates.md.
Assigned sub-agents:

- Architecture: Archimedes the 2nd.
- Clean Code / functional purity: Pauli the 2nd.
- Tests/TDD and verification: Nietzsche the 2nd.
- Security: Godel the 2nd.
- Release/licensing: Cicero the 2nd.
- Reusable runtime/components: Goodall the 2nd.

Scope decision:

- M3-002B is trusted, pure SCI eval only. It does not claim full Clojure
  support, untrusted-user scripting support, host function projection, raw Java
  interop, raw IO/process/env access, raw classpath/deps support, or arbitrary
  Babashka compatibility.
- Public `ecritum_*` value/job/call handles remain owned by the C wrapper.
  Native Image may expose private backend entrypoints only; no public
  Clojure-specific ABI symbols are added in this slice.
- Existing ADR-005 and ADR-021 cover the runtime and ABI decisions. A new ADR is
  required before implementation only if this slice changes public ABI, job
  semantics, host projection scope, raw SCI/Graal option exposure, distribution
  contents beyond SCI/transitives, or user-facing support claims.

Release dependency acceptance:

- Clojars checked on 2026-06-05 lists `org.babashka/sci` `0.12.51`, EPL-1.0,
  and dependencies `borkdude/edamame` `1.5.37`, `borkdude/graal.locking`
  `0.0.2`, `org.babashka/sci.impl.types` `0.0.2`, and
  `org.clojure/clojure` `1.10.3`.
- The implementation records Clojars repository acceptance, exact dependency
  tree, SPDX license mapping including EPL-1.0, manual acceptance for
  `sci.impl.types`, dependency-delta baseline, and artifact/license gate output.

Implementation record:

- `native/pom.xml` pins SCI `0.12.51` and Maven uses the Clojars repository
  required for SCI transitive artifacts.
- Native Image exposes private backend entrypoint
  `_ecritum_graal_eval_clojure`; the public ABI remains language-neutral.
- Production `ecritum_eval_start` copies borrowed script inputs before return,
  creates a detached worker thread, and uses condition-backed job wait/result
  state instead of evaluating synchronously on the caller thread.
- Eval is fail-closed for unsupported languages, non-empty raw options JSON, and
  runtime `languages` configuration that does not include Clojure.
- Structured script diagnostics now include public accessors for error
  category, operation, language, and source name; Swift copies those details
  before destroying the native error handle.
- SCI result conversion covers scalar, array, object, nil, bool, string,
  integer, and double values through the M3-002A value ABI.
- SCI source policy rejects duplicate normalized map keys, denies conservative
  dangerous source fragments, and redacts URL/token/password/secret/API-key
  diagnostics before crossing the native boundary.

Review record:

- Architecture persona: PASS after async worker/job wait, fail-closed language
  handling, and private-symbol guard fixes.
- Clean Code persona: PASS after extracting the source-deny policy, rejecting
  duplicate normalized map keys, and making language/options behavior explicit.
- Tests/TDD persona: PASS after Java, C ABI, ASan, native artifact, XCFramework,
  Swift, ABI, dependency, and release-report gates were added to the aggregate
  verification path.
- Security persona: PASS for trusted pure SCI eval after fail-closed
  language/config/options behavior and redacted diagnostics tests.
- Release persona: PASS for SCI dependency inventory and artifact evidence.
  Remaining release blockers are not M3-002B functional blockers: artifact size
  exceeds budget and two existing shipped-license entries remain NOASSERTION.
- Claude plan/diff review was invoked directly with `claude -p` and no auth
  check, as required. Calls hung with no output and were killed, including the
  final 2026-06-05 tool-less diff review attempt. Do not count Claude as
  signoff for this task; use the persona review record plus this blocker note.

Definition of done:

- DONE `native/pom.xml` pins SCI `0.12.51` and records dependency/license
  impact.

  and double values through the M3-002A value ABI.

  category, operation, language, and source name.
- DONE Native Image and artifact smoke tests pass.

  and accept the exact SCI dependency tree for this slice.

**** DONE M3-002C Project host functions into SCI

Lead persona: GraalVM Runtime.
Reviewer personas: Security, Architecture, Clean Code, Tests/TDD, Release.
Write scope: native/, Sources/, Tests/, Tests/Conformance/,
Tests/Security/.
Assigned sub-agents:

- Architecture: Mencius the 2nd.
- Security: Euclid the 2nd.
- Clean Code / functional core: Confucius the 2nd.
- Tests/TDD and verification: Maxwell the 2nd.
- Release/GraalVM Runtime: Boole the 2nd.

Planning status:

- 2026-06-05: Engineering manager started M3-002C after M3-002B was marked
  done. Fresh persona agents are reviewing architecture, security, clean-code,
  verification, and release/GraalVM risks before implementation.
- 2026-06-05: Claude plan consult was invoked directly with `claude -p`, with
  no auth check, and timed out after 45 seconds with no review output. Do not
  count Claude as signoff unless a later bounded retry returns usable feedback.
- 2026-06-05: Persona planning review completed. Architecture, Security, Clean
  Code, Tests/TDD, and Release/GraalVM all found the same implementation
  blocker: production SCI has no host projection bridge and the current callback
  invocation evidence is test-only. Accepted direction is a private Native Image
  callback-pointer bridge, copied host-projection manifest, shared C invocation
  helper, synchronous eval-worker callbacks, active projection pinning, and real
  native/Swift/conformance/security tests.
- 2026-06-05: ADR-021 was updated with an M3-002C host-projection addendum for
  Clojure projection syntax, private bridge shape, projection lifetime, callback
  thread/reentry behavior, value-kind coverage, and callback error mapping.

Pre-implementation plan:

- Keep the public C ABI unchanged. Host projection must use only existing
  public namespace/function/call/value handles and private runtime entrypoints.
- Add a private Native Image eval entrypoint that accepts a private C callback
  function pointer plus an opaque runtime handle. The C wrapper passes these
  only for production Clojure eval.
- SCI exposes only explicitly registered Ecritum namespace/function pairs as
  callable functions. No raw Java lookup, class loading, process, filesystem,
  network, environment, raw C handle, or unrestricted host object access is
  introduced by this task.
- Java encodes host-call arguments as the existing backend value wire format.
  The private C bridge resolves the registered function for the runtime,
  creates a normal `ecritum_call_t`, invokes the existing `ecritum_host_fn_t`
  callback with ADR-019 lifetime/reentry rules, validates the returned
  `ecritum_value_t`, and encodes either the result value or a structured
  callback/permission error back to SCI.
- Move the existing test-only callback invocation implementation into a shared
  internal helper so production host calls and `ECRITUM_TESTING` use the same
  ownership, active-call, result-validation, and cleanup behavior.
- Add C, Java, Swift, Native Image, XCFramework, conformance, and security
  tests before marking this task done.
- Add or update a real Clojure conformance provider so strict host/eval/error
  conformance is backed by the packaged runtime rather than fixture
  `pending_capability` results.
- Fix release docs drift: `release-check` now runs first-eval evidence, so
  `docs/release-gates.md` must not say first-eval is omitted from release check.

Definition of done:

- Registered host namespaces/functions are callable from Clojure only through
  explicit ADR-019 projection.
- Host callback arguments/results use public Ecritum call/value accessors.
- Callback failure maps to `ECRITUM_ERROR_CALLBACK` and denied host projection
  paths remain denied.
- Strict Clojure conformance host/eval/error cases pass with no required
  pending cases introduced by M3-002C.

Implementation notes:

- Added a private Native Image entrypoint
  `_ecritum_graal_eval_clojure_with_host` for Clojure eval with host
  projections. The public C ABI remains unchanged.
- Added a copied host-projection manifest from registered namespace/function
  pairs and active projection pinning so projected functions cannot be
  destroyed while an eval job is using them.
- Moved callback invocation into a shared internal C helper used by production
  host projection and the `ECRITUM_TESTING` callback evidence path.
- SCI now exposes only explicitly registered projected host functions and uses
  the backend value wire format for host arguments/results, including data
  values.
- Added conservative deny probes for dynamic resolution/eval/import/new/interop
  paths before host callbacks can be reached.
- Added artifact-backed Swift eval coverage for registered Swift host
  callbacks, callback argument reads, data return values, and callback failure
  mapping.
- Added `Tests/Conformance/fixtures/clojure_native_provider.py`, a packaged
  XCFramework-backed Clojure provider for strict eval/host/error conformance.
- Fixed release-gate documentation drift around first-eval evidence.

Review status:

- Persona planning review completed before implementation. Architecture,
  Security, Clean Code, Tests/TDD, and Release/GraalVM all agreed on the
  private callback-pointer bridge, copied projection manifest, active
  projection pinning, shared invocation helper, and real native/Swift/
  conformance/security tests.
- Claude plan consult timed out after 45 seconds with no review output.
- Claude post-change review was invoked directly with `claude -p` and no auth
  check on 2026-06-05; it timed out after 75 seconds with no output. Do not
  count Claude as signoff for M3-002C.

Verification evidence:

- `python3 -m py_compile Tests/Conformance/fixtures/clojure_native_provider.py
  scripts/run-conformance.py` -> PASS.
- `python3 -m json.tool Tests/Conformance/manifest.json >/dev/null` -> PASS.
- `mise exec -- just test-java` -> PASS; 17 Java tests.
- `mise exec -- just native` -> PASS; generated 29.86 MB Native Image dylib
  and exported `_ecritum_graal_eval_clojure_with_host`.
- `mise exec -- just test-c-abi-eval` and
  `mise exec -- just test-c-abi-eval-asan` -> PASS.
- `mise exec -- just test-native-eval-smoke` and
  `mise exec -- just test-native-eval-smoke-asan` -> PASS.
- `mise exec -- just xcframework` -> PASS.
- `mise exec -- just test-xcframework-eval-smoke` -> PASS; 57 Swift tests.
- `mise exec -- just conformance-clojure-native` -> PASS; strict packaged
  Clojure eval/host/error provider passed 6 cases with 0 pending.
- `mise exec -- just conformance` -> PASS; 23 runner tests.
- `mise exec -- just check-abi` -> PASS.
- `mise exec -- just security` -> PASS; 22 security tests plus static, abuse,
  and parser-abuse gates.
- `mise exec -- just test-m3-002c` -> PASS end to end, including native build,
  Java tests, C/ASAN/native/Swift/conformance/security/ABI/license/dependency
  gates.

Remaining blockers and debt:

  later Claude retry returns usable output.
- Strict Clojure conformance here covers eval/host/error only. Permission,
  timeout, filesystem-root, and broader Babashka compatibility remain pending

*** DONE M3-003 Implement first standard-library facades

Lead persona: Security.
Reviewer personas: GraalVM Runtime, Clean Code, Tests, Unix.
Depends on: M3-002.
Write scope: native/, Tests/, docs/.

Assigned sub-agents:

- Security: Lovelace the 2nd.
- GraalVM Runtime: Gibbs the 2nd.
- Clean Code / functional core: Epicurus the 2nd.
- Tests/TDD and verification: Linnaeus the 2nd.
- Unix/reusable tooling: Carver the 2nd.

Planning status:

- 2026-06-05: Engineering manager started M3-003 in a fresh `jj` change on top
  of completed M3-002. M3-002C's completed persona agents were closed before
  assigning fresh M3-003 agents.
- 2026-06-05: Claude pre-implementation consult was invoked directly with
  `claude -p`, with no auth check, and timed out after 75 seconds with no
  review output. Do not count Claude as signoff unless a later bounded retry
  returns usable feedback.
- 2026-06-05: Local research found the Swift/C policy schema and C config parser
  already model filesystem roots, network rules, and clock/random/log toggles,
  but `SciClojureEvaluator` currently has no policy-aware `ecritum.*` facade
  and receives no effective policy snapshot.
- 2026-06-05: Persona planning review completed. Security, GraalVM Runtime,
  Clean Code, Tests/TDD, and Unix all blocked direct implementation until the
  facade contracts and private effective-policy bridge are documented in an ADR.
  Every persona attempted Claude directly; all Claude attempts timed out with no
  usable output.
- 2026-06-05: Drafted `docs/adr/0022-standard-library-facades.md` as the
  proposed M3-003 decision record and sent it to the same M3-003 persona agents
  plus Claude for review. Implementation remains blocked until ADR-022 is
  reviewed and accepted or revised.
- 2026-06-05: ADR-022 first review completed. Security, GraalVM Runtime, Clean
  Code, Tests/TDD, and Unix found blockers in exact `require` grammar,
  filesystem canonicalization/TOCTOU proof, HTTP scope, private bridge
  contract, JSON edge cases, module boundaries, strict zero-pending
  conformance/security gates, deterministic target outputs, and manifest
  schema. Patched ADR-022 to define those items and make HTTP default-deny-only
  for M3-003.
- 2026-06-05: ADR-022 second review passed. Claude returned PASS and all five
  M3-003 persona agents returned PASS, confirming prior blockers were resolved.
  Marked ADR-022 Accepted. Implementation may proceed against ADR-022.

Pre-implementation planning notes:

- M3-003 needs an ADR or ADR-005/ADR-004 addendum before implementation because
  it creates script-visible standard-library APIs and policy-enforced host side
  effects.
- The likely first implementation slice should keep `ecritum.json` pure and
  deterministic, keep `ecritum.time` deterministic unless clock is explicitly
  granted, and treat `ecritum.fs`/`ecritum.http` as facade APIs whose denied
  paths are implemented before any side-effecting allowed paths.
- Java must not receive raw C handles, raw Swift callbacks, or raw host objects.
  If policy data crosses into the backend, it should be a copied private
  manifest with pure policy decisions and named adapters.
- Filesystem allowed-root behavior must be race-aware enough for the support
  claim: normalize paths, deny traversal outside configured roots, and do not
  expose raw `clojure.java.io` or `babashka.fs`.
  Verification for allowed roots must use fixture directories, not ambient host
  paths.
- HTTP support should not add a broad HTTP client dependency or raw Java network
  access without a reviewed ADR decision. Denied-by-default behavior can land
  before allowed network side effects.
- Accepted namespace shape for planning: `ecritum.json/read-string`,
  `ecritum.json/write-string`, `ecritum.time/parse-instant`,
  `ecritum.time/format-instant`, `ecritum.time/now`, `ecritum.fs/read-text`,
  `ecritum.fs/read-bytes`, `ecritum.fs/exists?`, and `ecritum.http/request`.
- Runtime direction: install `ecritum.*` through SCI `:namespaces`, but do not
  rely on the current blanket `(require` denial forever because supported
  namespaces must be require-able per ADR-005.
- Clean-code direction: keep SCI vars thin and route through pure
  `StandardLibraryPolicy` decisions plus named adapters for filesystem, HTTP,
  clock, and JSON value conversion. Avoid reparsing policy JSON in Java and
  avoid growing `SciClojureEvaluator` into the full facade runtime.
- Test direction: start red in Java for namespace/facade semantics, then prove
  the artifact path with native C and Swift XCFramework smoke tests. Add
  `test-facades-clojure`, `conformance-clojure-facades`,
  `security-clojure-facades`, and a composed `test-m3-003` target.
- Conformance/security direction: extend the existing JSON runner protocols and
  providers rather than adding one-off facade tools. Strict facade conformance
  should cover JSON, time, filesystem default-deny, filesystem inside/outside
  root, and HTTP default-deny. Security abuse should replace fixture pending
  evidence with Clojure-native probes for raw IO/network/JDK escape hatches and
  facade traversal/symlink cases.

Definition of done:

- Filesystem is denied by default and allowed only under configured roots.
- Time/json/http behavior has deterministic tests.
- Permission errors are explicit and documented.

Implementation record:

- 2026-06-05: Implemented ADR-022 standard-library facades for Clojure/SCI:
  `ecritum.json`, `ecritum.time`, `ecritum.fs`, and default-deny-only
  `ecritum.http`.
- 2026-06-05: Added a private Native Image entrypoint
  `ecritum_graal_eval_clojure_with_stdlib` and wired the C runtime wrapper to
  pass a copied effective-policy manifest plus a private side-effect callback.
  The public C ABI remains unchanged.
- 2026-06-05: Kept JSON/time pure in Java; kept filesystem side effects in C
  behind configured roots with canonicalization, `O_NOFOLLOW`, post-open path
  revalidation, size caps, and UTF-8 validation for `read-text`.
- 2026-06-05: Added native, Swift, conformance, security, and `just` gates for
  facade behavior, exact supported requires, default denials, allowed-root
  success, outside-root denial, traversal denial, and symlink escape denial.
- 2026-06-05: Added a native symbol check for the private stdlib entrypoint in
  `check-native`.

Review record:

- 2026-06-05: Persona implementation review found blockers in reserved aliases,
  JSON surrogate handling, unknown policy keys, duplicate filesystem roots,
  source-name propagation, native symbol verification, structured overflow
  errors, and test coverage. Fixed those issues before final acceptance.
- 2026-06-05: Accepted the remaining Clean Code concern about internal stdlib
  bridge/require/normalization seams as `ECRITUM-DEBT-0008`; it does not change
  the public ABI or M3-003 behavior claim and is scheduled for the M4.5
  clean-code pass.
- 2026-06-05: Tool-less Claude post-change review was invoked directly with
  `claude -p` and no auth check; it produced no review content due to a bounded
  wrapper failure, so it was not counted as signoff.
- 2026-06-05: Read-only Claude implementation review was invoked directly with
  `claude -p` and no auth check; it returned PASS with no blockers. Minor
  non-blocking notes: Java policy error paths are mostly integration-covered,
  `time.now` remains deny-only, and race coverage is represented by post-open
  fail-closed containment evidence.

Verification evidence:

- `mise exec -- just test-m3-003` -> PASS on 2026-06-05. This included
  `native`, `test-java`, `test-c-abi-eval`, `test-c-abi-eval-asan`,
  `test-c-abi-policy-config`, `test-c-abi-policy-config-asan`,

** Milestone M4.5: ABI Freeze and Packaged App Smoke

Goal: freeze the first public ABI candidate after Clojure and JavaScript prove
the runtime model.

Lead: Architecture Expert.
Required reviewers: Swift DX, Release, Tests, Security.

Definition of done:

- ABI versioning and compatibility ADR is accepted.
- Public C symbol manifest is checked in and reviewed.
- Public C symbols and Swift APIs are documented.
- ThreadSanitizer, leak checks, and lifecycle stress tests pass where practical.
- A packaged macOS app smoke test loads the runtime without external runtimes.

  (`docs: plan ABI freeze policy`) on top of completed M4-002.
- 2026-06-05: Claude plan consult invoked directly with `claude -p` and no
  auth-check step. The bounded compact prompt timed out with no output; do not
  count Claude as plan signoff.
- 2026-06-05: Drafted `docs/adr/0012-abi-versioning-and-compatibility-policy.md`
  as Proposed. The draft treats `docs/abi/ecritum-c-abi.json` as the freeze
  ledger, allows additive runtime behavior behind existing symbols, blocks
  optional new public C symbols until an ABI query path exists, and assigns
  manifest-schema expansion to the M4.5 freeze follow-up.
- 2026-06-05: Accepted ADR-012. The ADR is policy-complete, not
  freeze-complete: freeze-grade manifest/checker hardening is split into
  M4.5-001A before packaged app smoke begins.

Definition of done:

- ADR defines symbol naming, version checks, compatibility policy, deprecation,
  and breaking-change process.
- `just check-abi` is the verification path.

Review:

- Architecture review: PASS for policy acceptance. Required follow-up: manifest
  must cover typedefs, structs, callbacks, value kinds, job states, private
  symbol patterns, ABI query policy, extra-export checks, release docs, and
  Mach-O compatibility metadata before ABI freeze is claimed.
- Tests/TDD review: PASS for ADR acceptance only if `ecritum_version` remains a
  product version and manifest/check hardening is required before freeze.
  `mise exec -- just check-abi` passed, but current coverage is not
  freeze-grade.
- Swift DX / Release review: PASS for policy acceptance. Release blocker before
  M4.5-002: harden `check-abi`; Swift currently checks artifact presence and
  `ecritum_version`, not ABI compatibility, so typed old-artifact failure is
  deferred to the freeze-hardening follow-up.
- Claude plan consult: initial bounded prompt timed out. Final compact ADR
  status review returned PASS: no blocker to marking ADR-012 accepted as policy
  with freeze hardening tracked separately.

*** DONE M4.5-001A Harden ABI manifest and check-abi for freeze

Lead persona: Tests/TDD.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Swift DX, Release, Security.
Depends on: M4.5-001.
Write scope: docs/abi/, scripts/, Tests/, Sources/CEcritum/include/ecritum.h,
Sources/Ecritum/.

Definition of done:

- `docs/abi/ecritum-c-abi.json` covers public functions, status constants,
  value kinds, job states, public typedefs, public structs, callback types,
  buffer constants, private-symbol patterns, and packaged-slice expectations.
- `just check-abi` rejects extra public exports, missing declarations,
  renumbered constants, header drift, private symbol leaks, and manifest/header/
  Java/Swift status divergence.
- Packaged header equality and all shipped slices are checked.
- The release pipeline's Mach-O `current_version` and `compatibility_version`
  policy is tied to ADR-012 or explicitly documented as pre-release metadata.
- Swift has either a typed runtime-artifact ABI mismatch failure path or an
  accepted deferral that blocks external release candidates.
- Verification includes negative checker fixtures, C/C++ header smoke, packaged
  `check-abi`, Swift status mapping tests, and reviewer signoff.

Notes:

- Expanded `docs/abi/ecritum-c-abi.json` from a function/status list into the
  M4.5 freeze ledger: C/Java/Swift status mappings, Swift job states, buffer
  constants, value kinds, job states, public handle typedefs, public structs,
  callback signatures, all public functions, exact private symbols, private
  symbol regexes, packaged header path, and pre-release Mach-O version metadata.
- Hardened `scripts/check-abi.sh` so it validates manifest/header/Java/Swift
  parity, rejects unmanifested public header functions, checks public typedefs,
  structs, callbacks, constants, and functions, scans every packaged
  `EcritumRuntime.framework` slice, checks packaged header equality, rejects
  extra `_ecritum_*` exports and private leak patterns, and validates the
  framework `LC_ID_DYLIB` current/compatibility version metadata.
- Added `Tests/ABI/test_check_abi.py` with fake `nm`/`otool` fixtures covering
  valid slices plus negative cases for extra public export, private symbol
  pattern leak, packaged header drift, C constant renumbering, Swift status
  drift, and callback signature drift.
- Accepted deferral: no ABI query symbol and no typed old-artifact mismatch
  implementation in this task. ADR-012 keeps both as external release-candidate
  blockers before optional public C symbols or external RC claims.

Review:

- Architecture review: PASS checklist; required manifest/checker coverage was
  implemented.
- Swift DX / Release review: PASS checklist; all-slice packaged header equality,
  Mach-O pre-release metadata, Swift status parity, and external-RC old-artifact
  deferral were addressed.
- Security review: PASS checklist; extra `_ecritum_*` export rejection and
  private regex leak checks were implemented with negative fixtures.
- Claude final compact implementation review: PASS; no blockers, accepted the
  ABI query and old-artifact compatibility paths as correctly deferred.

  Lua installs.

- Swift DX leads a minimal Swift executable under `Examples/MacSmokeApp` using
  the public Swift API.
- Release/Unix packaging is a reusable script that builds the example,
  assembles `EcritumSmoke.app`, copies the matching XCFramework slice into
  `Contents/Frameworks`, adds the app-bundle rpath, and checks Mach-O install
  names.
- Tests/Security verification runs the app through a sanitized environment with
  no `DYLD_*` overrides and rejects workspace-local, GraalVM, JDK, native build,
  or language-runtime install paths in the app's link metadata.

- Swift DX lead: packaged app example source and Swift API ergonomics.
- Release/Unix review: bundle layout, rpath, install names, reusable `just`
  target.
- Tests/Security review: Clojure/JavaScript smoke coverage, sanitized
  environment, external runtime path rejection.

Notes:
