  requires the runtime artifact, registers a Swift host callback, and evaluates
  Clojure plus JavaScript scripts through the Swift API.

  assembles `EcritumSmoke.app`, copies the matching
  `EcritumRuntime.framework` slice into `Contents/Frameworks`, adds the
  app-bundle rpath, signs and verifies the bundle when `codesign` is available,
  relocates the bundle outside the repository, runs it through `env -i` with an
  empty `PATH`, and checks Mach-O install names for bundled runtime paths only.
- Added a negative packaging check: after relocation, removing the bundled
  `EcritumRuntime.framework` must make the app launch fail.
- Added `just packaged-app-smoke` / `just test-packaged-app-smoke`, included
  the packaged app smoke in `just examples`, and added it to
  `scripts/release-check.sh`.

- Swift DX review: recommended Swift API smoke through an app bundle and host
  callback coverage; implemented.
- Release/Unix review: recommended relocation outside the repo, app-bundle
  rpath checks, no `DYLD_*` dependency, broken-bundle negative check, and a
  `test-packaged-app-smoke` target; implemented except sandbox-exec, which
  remains outside this smoke's scope.
- Tests/Security review: recommended Clojure and JavaScript execution plus
  external runtime path rejection; implemented, with deeper abuse probes covered
  by existing conformance/security gates.
- Claude plan review: attempted directly with Claude CLI, but the CLI review
  session had filesystem tools disabled and returned no actionable file-level
  feedback.
- Claude implementation review: found one blocking source-layout concern
  (`@main` in `main.swift`); fixed by renaming the entry point to
  `EcritumSmokeApp.swift`.
- Claude second implementation review: PASS.

*** DONE M4.5-003 Resolve JavaScript nested host value conversion debt

Lead persona: Clean Code and Functional Core.
Reviewer personas: TDD/Testability, Architecture, Swift DX.
Debt: ECRITUM-DEBT-0010.
Depends on: M4-002, M4.5-002.
Write scope: native/src/main/java/ecritum/JavaScriptEvaluator.java,
native/src/test/java/ecritum/JavaScriptEvaluatorTest.java,
Tests/C/native_eval_smoke.c, Tests/EcritumTests/EcritumEvalTests.swift,
DEBT.md, PROJECT.org.

Definition of done:

- JavaScript host callback return values normalize correctly when arrays,
  objects, and data are returned top-level or nested inside guest-created
  JavaScript arrays/objects.
- Unsupported executable, promise, non-plain, cyclic, and ambient host-access
  values remain rejected.
- The change does not widen host capabilities, public C ABI, Swift API, or
  runtime support claims.
- Java, native C, and Swift artifact-backed tests cover nested host arrays,
  objects, and data.
- Claude plan and implementation reviews have been run directly with
  `claude -p`; auth checks are skipped because Claude CLI works in this repo.
- TDD/Testability and Clean Code persona reviews have been recorded.

Implementation plan:

- Start with Java regression tests that reproduce nested host-returned array,
  object, and data conversion failure.
- Keep conversion scoped to `JavaScriptEvaluator` unless the fix requires a
  separate `JavaScriptValueCodec`; avoid public API/ABI changes.
- Extend native C and Swift JavaScript host smokes after Java behavior is fixed
  and rebuild the local artifact if needed.
- Close ECRITUM-DEBT-0010 only after Java/native/Swift evidence passes.

Reviewer assignments:

- Clean Code lead: value normalization boundaries, proxy handling, and
  unsupported-result rejection.
- TDD/Testability review: Java/native/Swift regression coverage and verification
  commands.
- Architecture/Swift DX review: no public ABI/API widening and artifact-backed
  developer experience remains coherent.

Progress notes:

- 2026-06-06: Engineering Manager opened jj change `fix: convert nested
  JavaScript host values`, selected ECRITUM-DEBT-0010 as the next actionable
  debt item, and spawned fresh Clean Code plus TDD/Testability sub-agent reviews.
- 2026-06-06: Initial research found nested normalization is centralized in
  `JavaScriptEvaluator.normalizeValue`; top-level host array/data return tests
  already exist, but guest-object nesting needs source and artifact-backed
  coverage.

Planned verification:

- `mise exec -- mvn -s .mvn/settings.xml -f native/pom.xml
  -Dtest=JavaScriptEvaluatorTest test`
- `mise exec -- just test-java`
- `mise exec -- just native`
- `mise exec -- just test-native-eval-smoke`
- `mise exec -- just xcframework`
- `mise exec -- just test-swift`
- `mise exec -- just conformance-javascript-native`
- `mise exec -- just security-javascript`
- `mise exec -- just plan-check`

Notes:

- Added Java regression coverage for host-returned arrays, objects, and byte
  data nested inside guest-created JavaScript objects and arrays.
- Added Java rejection coverage for unsupported host return values and cyclic
  host lists/object arrays.
- Changed JavaScript host return conversion to materialize host lists/arrays as
  real guest JavaScript arrays and host maps as null-prototype JavaScript
  objects before returning to guest code. This keeps result normalization on
  guest values and avoids accepting arbitrary Graal proxy values.
- Updated the plain-object guard to accept null-prototype objects while
  continuing to reject non-plain values such as `Map`.
- Extended native C and Swift artifact-backed JavaScript host smokes with
  nested host-returned array/object/data assertions.
- No ADR was written: the change is internal codec behavior and does not alter
  public C ABI, Swift API, security policy, distribution shape, or support
  claims.

Review:

- Clean Code persona review: recommended materializing host lists/arrays as
  guest arrays and maps as null-prototype guest objects, rejecting cyclic host
  collections, avoiding broad proxy normalization, and adding C/Swift
  artifact-backed coverage. Implemented.
- TDD/Testability persona review: recommended Java, C/native, and Swift nested
  host-return tests and warned that C/Swift evidence must follow `just native`
  and `just xcframework`. Implemented.
- Claude plan review: direct `claude -p` attempts timed out with no output.
- Claude implementation review: direct `claude -p` attempt timed out after 120s
  with no output (`CLAUDE_STATUS=124`). Persona review was used as fallback and
  the timeout is recorded here.

*** DONE M4.5-004 Decouple Clojure standard-library seams

Lead persona: Clean Code and Functional Core.
Reviewer personas: TDD/Testability, Architecture, Security.
Debt: ECRITUM-DEBT-0008.
Depends on: M3-003, M4.5-003.
Write scope: native/src/main/java/ecritum/, native/src/test/java/ecritum/,
DEBT.md, PROJECT.org.

Definition of done:

- Literal supported `require` preprocessing is no longer implemented as nested
  parser classes inside `SciClojureEvaluator`.
- Clojure facade input/result normalization is owned by a dedicated internal
  value boundary rather than calling evaluator normalization from
  `StandardLibraryFacade`.
- `StandardLibraryBridge` returns an explicit backend result type or an ADR
  records why the current normalized-Java contract is intentionally retained.
- Behavior remains unchanged for supported `ecritum.*` requires, aliasing,
  denied require forms, JSON/time/fs/http facades, host projections, and
  security bypass probes.
- No public C ABI, Swift API, language support claim, runtime policy, or
  distribution behavior changes.
- Claude review attempts and persona reviews are recorded, with fallback noted
  if Claude CLI times out.

Implementation plan:

- Extract require rewriting into a dedicated internal class with focused tests
  covering allowed literal forms, aliases, strings/comments, malformed forms,
  and denied namespaces.
- Extract Clojure value normalization into a dedicated internal codec used by
  both evaluator result normalization and Clojure facade functions.
- Inspect `StandardLibraryBridge` call sites and either introduce an explicit
  bridge result wrapper or record a narrow acceptance if the current object
  contract is already the least risky internal boundary.
- Run Java tests first; run broader native/Swift smoke only if public behavior
  or artifact-backed facade behavior changes.

Reviewer assignments:

- Clean Code lead: internal seams, pure parsing/normalization helpers, naming.
- TDD/Testability review: focused regression tests and cheapest useful gates.
- Architecture/Security review: no public boundary widening and no denied
  require/capability regression.

Progress notes:

- 2026-06-06: Engineering Manager opened jj change `refactor: decouple clojure
  stdlib facades`, selected ECRITUM-DEBT-0008 as the next actionable internal
  cleanup, and spawned fresh Clean Code plus TDD/Testability sub-agent reviews.
- 2026-06-06: Initial research found `SciClojureEvaluator` owns require
  rewriting, `StandardLibraryFacade.FacadeFunction` calls
  `SciClojureEvaluator.normalizeValue`, and `StandardLibraryBridge` returns raw
  Java values from native stdlib callbacks.

Planned verification:

- `mise exec -- mvn -s .mvn/settings.xml -f native/pom.xml
  -Dtest=SciClojureEvaluatorTest test`

- `mise exec -- just security-clojure-facades`
- `mise exec -- just plan-check`

Notes:

- Extracted `SciRequirePreprocessor` and `SciRequireRewrite` so literal
  supported require preprocessing no longer lives inside `SciClojureEvaluator`.
- Extracted `ClojureValueCodec` and routed Clojure eval results, host-call
  arguments/results, and facade function results through that dedicated
  internal normalization boundary.
- Added `StandardLibraryResult` and changed `StandardLibraryBridge` to return
  explicit success/failure results. Clojure, JavaScript, and Lua facades now
  deliberately unwrap bridge results through `valueOrThrow`.
- Kept the public C ABI, Swift API, runtime policy, language support claims,
  and distribution behavior unchanged.
- No ADR was written: this is an internal clean-code boundary refactor with
  focused tests and no public contract change.

Review:

- Clean Code persona review: recommended extracting require rewriting,
  centralizing Clojure/SCI normalization in `ClojureValueCodec`, and
  strengthening `StandardLibraryResult` to carry success/failure status.

- `mise exec -- just test-m3-003` -> exit 0, including native rebuild, Java
  tests, C ABI eval/policy/native smoke tests, ASan variants, XCFramework
  rebuild/check, Swift artifact tests, Clojure facade conformance/security,
  broader security, ABI, license report, and dependency delta
- `mise exec -- just plan-check` -> exit 0
- `build/facades/clojure.json` -> `ok=true`
- `build/conformance/clojure-facades.json` -> `ok=true`
- `build/security/clojure-facades.json` -> `ok=true`
New tests added:
- `SciRequirePreprocessorTest`
- `ClojureValueCodecTest`
- `StandardLibraryResultTest`
- `SciClojureEvaluatorTest.mapsStandardLibraryBridgeResultsThroughFacades`
Negative paths tested:
- Malformed, dynamic, unsupported, `:refer`, mixed, and unsafe alias require
  forms are denied by the extracted preprocessor/evaluator path.
- Duplicate normalized map keys and unsupported Clojure values are rejected by
  the extracted value codec.
- Standard-library bridge permission, script, and internal failures propagate
  through the Clojure facade path without raw exception leakage.
Size impact:
- Native image rebuilt at 152.19MB total file size; no release budget decision
  changed in this task.
Sanitizers:
- `just test-m3-003` ran C ABI eval, policy, and native eval ASan/UBSan smoke
  variants.
Not verified:
- Public release signing/notarization and hosted consumer smoke; outside this
  internal cleanup and still owned by M7 release gates.

** DONE Milestone M5: Lua Feasibility and Runtime Decision

Goal: decide whether Lua ships in the default artifact through LuaJ or another
implementation.

Lead: GraalVM Runtime.
Required reviewers: Architecture, Tests, Security, Release.

Definition of done:

- ADR compares LuaJ, Rembulan, Cobalt, and separate native Lua options.
- Native Image feasibility is tested.
- If accepted, Lua smoke tests pass and size delta is recorded.
- If rejected or deferred, the public roadmap and docs avoid false support
  claims.
- Spike code is hardened with tests or removed.

Milestone result:

- M5-001 is DONE. LuaJ compiled into the Native Image shared library, Lua smoke
  and abuse tests pass, size/perf/license impact is recorded, and ADR-0023
  keeps Lua experimental until Core/Full classification and memory controls are
  resolved.

*** DONE M5-001 Spike LuaJ in Native Image

Lead persona: GraalVM Runtime.
Reviewer personas: Tests, Security, Release.
Write scope: native/, Tests/, docs/adr/, scripts/, justfile, PROJECT.org,
DEBT.md, docs/release-gates.md.

Definition of done:

- LuaJ compiles into the shared library or failure is documented with evidence.
- Smoke tests cover eval, values, host calls, errors, timeout, and permissions.
- ADR decides default artifact inclusion or deferral.

Implementation plan:

- Use `org.luaj:luaj-jme:3.0.1` from Maven Central, not `luaj-jse`, to avoid
  the JSE Luajava bridge classes in the first adapter.
- Add `LuaEvaluator` with custom LuaJ globals, internal DebugLib instruction
  budget hook, and guest-visible removal of `debug`, `package`, `require`,
  `dofile`, `loadfile`, `load`, `loadstring`, `coroutine`, and `string.dump`;
  omit `CoroutineLib` until a hook-bypass review proves it safe.
- Add private Native Image entrypoint `ecritum_graal_eval_lua_with_stdlib` and
  route `"lua"` through the existing public eval/job/value ABI.
- Extend Java/native/conformance/security tests before claiming support.
- Update shipped dependency/license inventory and dependency delta for LuaJ.
- Record size/perf evidence; Lua remains an experimental measured candidate
  until artifact classification is resolved.

Review:

- Release review: LuaJ must be shipped MIT inventory, `check-dep-delta` must
  change only with review, size/perf data are required, and Lua cannot silently
  become Core while ADR-018 size gates already fail.
- Release gating update: `org.luaj:luaj-jme:3.0.1` is accepted as a shipped MIT
  experimental dependency with no transitive runtime dependencies. M5-001
  verification proved `CoroutineLib` is omitted and `string.dump`/binary chunks
  are denied. Lua Core promotion remains blocked on ADR-018/Core-Full
  classification and a memory-limiting plan for untrusted Lua workloads.
- Tests/Security review: support claim requires strict eval/value/host/error/
  timeout/permission coverage and denial of LuaJ escape hatches including
  Luajava, Java classes, IO/OS/debug/package/require/load, native loading,
  process/env, and bytecode/classpath mutation.
- Tests/Security fixture preparation: added Lua native conformance and abuse
  providers scoped to the packaged XCFramework. Coverage probes now include
  eval scalar/array/object, host callback, script error, timeout, standard
  library default-deny/allowed-root cases, and LuaJ-specific escape hatches for
  Luajava/Java lookup, IO/OS/debug/package/require/loadfile/dofile/load/
  loadstring/string.dump, collectgarbage, and coroutine budget bypass attempts.
- Claude fixture review attempts: scoped diff review was interrupted after the
  CLI stalled without output; scoped read-only consult exited by `timeout 120`
  with no JSON response. No Claude findings were available for this fixture
  handoff.
- Tests/Security fixture verification:
  - `python3 -m py_compile Tests/Conformance/fixtures/lua_native_provider.py
    Tests/Security/fixtures/lua_abuse_provider.py` -> exit 0.
  - `python3 scripts/run-security-abuse.py --manifest
    Tests/Security/abuse-manifest.json --validate-manifest` -> exit 0, 68 cases.
  - Forced missing-artifact contract checks for both Lua providers -> exit 0.
  - Not verified by this subtask: strict `conformance-lua-native` and
    `security-lua` against the packaged artifact; owner is the runtime
    integration task after the Lua native entrypoint and XCFramework are rebuilt.
- Implementation result: LuaJ compiled into the Native Image shared library
  through `org.luaj:luaj-jme:3.0.1`; the public C ABI stayed unchanged and the
  only new native symbol is private: `ecritum_graal_eval_lua_with_stdlib`.
- Timeout-state correction: backend `ECRITUM_ERROR_TIMEOUT` now maps to
  `ECRITUM_JOB_TIMED_OUT`, matching ADR-003/ADR-014.
- Runtime verification:
  - `mise exec -- just test-java` -> exit 0, 44 tests including 10 Lua adapter
    tests.
  - `mise exec -- just native` -> exit 0; Native Image size 152.18 MB, LuaJ JME
    code area about 542.6 KB.
  - `mise exec -- just test-native-eval-smoke` -> exit 0.
  - `mise exec -- just test-native-eval-smoke-asan` -> exit 0.
  - `mise exec -- just xcframework` -> exit 0.
  - `mise exec -- just test-swift` -> exit 0, 65 runtime tests including Lua
    Swift artifact tests.
  - `mise exec -- just conformance-lua-native` -> exit 0, 13/13 strict cases.
  - `mise exec -- just security-lua` -> exit 0, 68/68 strict abuse probes.
  - `mise exec -- just check-abi` -> exit 0.
  - `mise exec -- just check-xcframework` -> exit 0.
  - `mise exec -- just test-security-static` -> exit 0.
  - `mise exec -- just license-report` -> exit 0; LuaJ JME is MIT and
    non-blocking.
  - `mise exec -- just check-dep-delta` -> exit 0.
  - `mise exec -- just inspect` -> exit 0; embedded runtime list includes LuaJ
    JME.
  - `mise exec -- just size` -> expected exit 1 under ADR-018: artifact
    152,317,307 bytes and private runtime 152,175,352 bytes exceed Core budgets;
    wrapper 130,096 bytes stays within budget.
  - `mise exec -- just bench-cold-start` -> exit 0; startup process elapsed p50
    18.317 ms, p95 60.483 ms; first call p95 9.017 ms.
  - `mise exec -- just bench-idle-rss` -> exit 0; RSS after call p95
    15,810,560 bytes.
  - `mise exec -- just bench-lua-first-eval` -> exit 0; Lua first eval p50
    1.006 ms, p95 1.835 ms.
  - `mise exec -- just license-report-strict` -> expected exit 1 only for the
    pre-existing `EcritumRuntime.xcframework` and GraalVM Native Image embedded
    runtime `NOASSERTION` shipped-license blockers.
- Claude plan review: BLOCKER until the adapter avoids LuaJ coroutine budget
  bypasses and strips `string.dump`. Engineering-manager decision: omit
  `CoroutineLib`, deny coroutine probes, strip `string.dump`, and track heap
  allocation limits as a follow-up before any Core promotion.
- Claude implementation review: full-diff review stalled with no output and was
  interrupted; scoped Lua implementation review returned PASS with no blockers.
  Residual risks were LuaJ age, no heap accounting, BaseLib surface, and regex
  denial being defense-in-depth rather than enforcement; these are accepted by
  ADR-0023/ECRITUM-DEBT-0011 while Lua remains experimental.
- GraalVM Runtime review: recommended the existing dedicated-evaluator/private
  entrypoint pattern and initially suggested `luaj-jse`; engineering manager
  resolved this to `luaj-jme` after local jar inspection found JSE Luajava
  bridge classes unnecessary for the M5 adapter.
- Local feasibility probes: custom LuaJ globals evaluated `return 40 + 2`,
  hid `debug`/`package`, and interrupted `while true do end` with an internal
  DebugLib instruction hook.

** DONE Milestone M6: Python and Ruby Gates

Goal: test whether GraalPy and TruffleRuby are practical for the default
artifact or should become optional/full artifacts.

Lead: GraalVM Runtime.
Required reviewers: Release, Tests, Security, Architecture.

Definition of done:

- Separate ADRs cover GraalPy and TruffleRuby inclusion gates.
- Native Image builds, resource packaging, size, startup, and license data are
  measured.
- Default artifact policy is decided before support is claimed.
- Spike code is hardened with tests or removed.

Milestone result:

- M6-001 and M6-002 are DONE. ADR-008 and ADR-009 reject GraalPy and
  TruffleRuby from the default Core artifact for v0 and keep both as
  Full-artifact candidates. Python/Ruby Native Image adapter builds were not
  run because the gate decisions rejected default inclusion before
  implementation; future Full-artifact spikes own those proofs.

*** DONE M6-001 Gate GraalPy inclusion

Lead persona: GraalVM Runtime.
Reviewer personas: Release, Security, Tests.
Write scope: native/, Tests/, docs/adr/.

Definition of done:

- Python stdlib packaging is proven or rejected.
- Pure-Python package loading policy is documented.
- Native wheels are explicitly non-goal for v0.

Execution plan:

- Engineering Manager started M6-001 in jj child change
  =docs: gate GraalPy inclusion= on top of completed M5-001.
- Lead persona: GraalVM and Polyglot Runtime Engineer.
- Reviewer personas: Release/Licensing, Security/Sandboxing,
  TDD/Testability, and Architecture.
- ADR requirement: write ADR-008 before any GraalPy support claim or runtime
  adapter implementation.
- Research checklist:
  - Read PLAN.org Python sections and current ADRs that constrain language
    inclusion, artifact budgets, Java/host interop, permissions, and resource
    limits.
  - Read current official GraalPy Native Image and embedding documentation.
  - Inspect current Maven coordinates and dependency/resource packaging shape.
  - Compare against existing Clojure, JavaScript, and Lua adapter patterns.
- Verification plan:
  - If implementation/spike code is added, run Java tests, Native Image build,
    XCFramework build, ABI check, conformance/security checks, size, startup,
    idle RSS, first-eval, license inventory, and dependency delta gates.
  - If the gate is decided by ADR without adapter code, verify with
    =mise exec -- just plan-check= and task-specific source/doc consistency
    checks, and record unimplemented proof gaps explicitly.
- Claude review plan: run plan consult on the ADR/gate decision, apply
  feedback, run a post-change diff review, and record accepted residual risks.

Review:

- GraalVM Runtime review: PASS. Recommended rejecting GraalPy from default
  Core/v0 and deferring Python to a Full-artifact spike. Confirmed current C
  dispatch keeps `python` runtime-unavailable and that current GraalPy Maven
  coordinates are `org.graalvm.polyglot:python` plus optional
  `org.graalvm.python:python-embedding` resource tooling.
- Security review: PASS. Required deny-by-default context settings, denial of
  Java/Polyglot/ctypes/cffi/native-extension/process/socket/env/fs/POSIX escape
  hatches, and resource-limit tests before any support claim. Native extensions
  remain a v0 non-goal because they require native access, IO, and thread
  permissions incompatible with Ecritum's untrusted-scripting boundary.
- Release review: PASS with additions. ADR-008 now requires multi-license SPDX
  handling for GraalPy dependencies, reproducible package/checksum evidence,
  data-driven or verified Python runtime/resource inspection, and explicit
  macOS slice policy because GraalVM 25.0.2 no longer supports macOS x64.
- Tests review: PASS. M6-001 should stay an ADR/research gate. Future support
  claim requires Python evaluator, C smoke, Swift artifact, conformance,
  security, static, size/perf/license/dependency gates.
- Claude plan consult: two scoped `claude -p` attempts timed out with no output
  and were recorded as unavailable for M6-001; no Claude findings were used.

Implementation result:

- Accepted ADR-008. GraalPy is not included in Ecritum Core and Ecritum must not
  claim Python support for v0 from M6-001.
- Python remains a Full-artifact candidate pending a later spike that proves
  Native Image shared-library packaging, XCFramework resource layout,
  conformance/security behavior, size/startup/RSS/first-eval impact, license
  inventory, dependency delta, reproducible packaging, clean-consumer behavior,
  and macOS slice policy.
- README and release gates now describe Python as gated/Full-candidate rather
  than supported.
- ECRITUM-DEBT-0005 was updated with the Python side of the Python/Ruby
  artifact policy; M6-002 owns the Ruby side.

  unless explicitly accepted, resource pruning/inventory for bundled gems and
  native/C-extension material, Core/Full dependency baselines, multi-license
  tooling, runtime/resource inspection, reproducible package checksums, and
  clean-consumer smoke before any Ruby claim.

  `Context.Builder` baseline and Ruby-specific probes for Java, Polyglot, inner
  contexts, Fiddle/FFI/NFI, C extensions/native gems, RubyGems/Bundler,
  `$LOAD_PATH`/`require`/`load`, raw IO/network/process/env, threads/Ractors,
  signal handlers, timeout/cancellation, and post-timeout context reuse.
- Tests review: PASS. M6-002 should stay an ADR/research gate. Future support
  claim requires Ruby evaluator, C smoke, Swift artifact, conformance, security,
  static, size/perf/license/dependency, reproducibility, and clean-consumer
  gates.
- Claude plan consult: scoped `claude -p` attempt timed out with no output in
  the main manager session and was recorded as unavailable; persona agents also
  attempted Claude where useful and reported no blocker changing the decision.

Implementation result:

- Accepted ADR-009. TruffleRuby is not included in Ecritum Core and Ecritum must
  not claim Ruby support for v0 from M6-002.
- Ruby remains a Full-artifact candidate pending a later spike that proves

  Image shared-library packaging, XCFramework resource layout,
  conformance/security behavior, size/startup/RSS/first-eval impact, license
  inventory, dependency delta, reproducible packaging, clean-consumer behavior,
  and macOS slice policy.
- README and release gates now describe Ruby as gated/Full-candidate rather
  than supported.
- ECRITUM-DEBT-0005 is resolved because ADR-008 and ADR-009 now own the
  remaining Python/Ruby Full-artifact proof gaps.

** Milestone M7: Distribution Hardening

Goal: make release artifacts trustworthy for SwiftPM consumers.

Lead: Release.
Required reviewers: Swift DX, Tests, Unix, Security, GraalVM Runtime.

Definition of done:

- macOS arm64 and x86_64 slices are built or documented as phased support.
- XCFramework is assembled, signed when required, zipped, and checksummed.
- License report and THIRD_PARTY_NOTICES.md are generated.
- Clean macOS consumer app runs without external runtimes.
- Size/startup/memory budget report is recorded.

*** DONE M7-001 Build release artifact pipeline

Lead persona: Release.
Reviewer personas: Unix, Tests, Swift DX.
Write scope: scripts/, justfile, docs/.

Definition of done:

- Packaging commands are reproducible.
- Checksums are generated for SwiftPM.
- Artifact contents are inspectable and documented.

Execution plan:

- Engineering Manager started M7-001 in jj child change
  =release: harden artifact pipeline= on top of completed M6-002.
- Lead persona: Release, Licensing, and Distribution Engineer.
- Reviewer personas: Unix, TDD/Testability, Swift DX, Security, GraalVM
  Runtime, and Architecture.
- ADR requirements: ADR-010 for XCFramework release/signing/checksum policy and
  ADR-017 for artifact reproducibility/signing/checksum policy must be accepted
  before changing release promises.
- Research checklist:
  - Read ADR-001, ADR-012, ADR-018, docs/release-gates.md, Package.swift,
    justfile, scripts/build-xcframework.sh, scripts/package-artifact.py,
    scripts/inspect-artifact.py, scripts/check-xcframework.sh, and current
    release-check flow.
  - Identify which release-pipeline capabilities already exist and which M7
    gaps remain.
  - Verify current package/checksum reproducibility before changing scripts.
- Verification plan:
  - `mise exec -- just plan-check`
  - `mise exec -- just xcframework`
  - `mise exec -- just check-xcframework`
  - `mise exec -- just inspect`
  - `mise exec -- just package-artifact` twice with checksum comparison
  - `mise exec -- just checksum`
  - `mise exec -- just release-check` or record expected failures with exact
    blockers
  - focused unit/script checks for any modified release tooling
- Claude review plan: run scoped plan consult after the release gaps are
  identified, apply feedback, then run a scoped diff review after changes.
- 2026-06-06 Release persona note: Claude read-only consult exited without
  usable output and a bounded tool-less retry timed out at 60 seconds. Do not
  count this as Claude signoff; rerun a scoped Claude review after ADR/script
  changes or record a fresh blocker.

Implementation summary:

- Accepted ADR-010 for XCFramework release, signing, and checksum policy.
- Accepted ADR-017 for deterministic package manifests, sidecar checksums, and
  reproducibility evidence.
- Added local ad-hoc signing to =build-xcframework.sh= by signing the nested
  private dylib first and the framework bundle second.
- Added signature verification to =check-xcframework.sh= and framework
  code-sign status to =inspect-artifact.py=.
- Replaced the static inspect runtime list with symbol-derived runtime
  inspection.
- Extended =package-artifact.py= to persist a JSON package manifest and checksum
  sidecar, including input artifact hash, per-file hashes, slices, and SwiftPM
  checksum.
- Added =check-package-reproducible.py= and =just package-artifact-verify= to
  package the same input twice and compare bytes, SHA-256, SwiftPM checksum,
  sidecar checksums, entry order, timestamps, compression, and metadata skips.
- Added release-mode manifest checks in =Package.swift= so partial
  URL/checksum configuration fails fast and =ECRITUM_RELEASE_RUNTIME_REQUIRED=1=
  forces =.binaryTarget(url:checksum:)= even when =dist/local= exists.
- Parameterized release-related =just= recipes for artifact/output reuse.
- Hardened =release-check.sh= with =--output-dir=, =--artifact=,
  =--release-zip=, =JUST= override, persisted package/repro/checksum/release
  manifest evidence, checksum shape validation, and sidecar comparison.
- Recorded =ECRITUM-DEBT-0012= for public Developer ID/notarization and hosted
  SwiftPM consumer enforcement, which belongs to later M7 release tasks.

*** DONE M7-002 Clean-machine consumer validation

Lead persona: Tests.
Reviewer personas: Release, Swift DX, Security.
Write scope: Examples/, Tests/, scripts/, docs/.

Definition of done:

- Consumer app builds and runs on a clean macOS environment.
- No GraalVM/JDK/language runtime install is required.
- Failures produce actionable diagnostics.

Execution plan:

- Engineering Manager started M7-002 in jj child change
  =test: validate clean SwiftPM consumer= on top of completed M7-001.
- Lead persona: TDD, Testability, and Verification Engineer.
- Reviewer personas: Release, Swift DX, Security, Unix, and Architecture.
- Scope: prove a clean external SwiftPM consumer can resolve Ecritum with
  =.binaryTarget(url:checksum:)= instead of the local path artifact, then run a
  small program without GraalVM/JDK/language runtime installation in the
  consumer project.
- Research checklist:
  - Read ADR-001, ADR-010, ADR-017, Package.swift, existing
    =Examples/MacSmokeApp=, =scripts/test-packaged-app-smoke.sh=,
    =scripts/package-artifact.py=, =scripts/release-check.sh=, and SwiftPM
    binary target behavior around URL/checksum artifacts.
  - Determine whether a local HTTP server, file URL, or generated consumer
    fixture is the safest reusable proof for CI.
  - Identify exact diagnostics for missing release zip, missing checksum,
    failed server startup, failed SwiftPM resolution, and runtime load failure.
- Verification plan:
  - =mise exec -- just plan-check=
  - focused script/unit checks for the new clean-consumer tooling
  - =mise exec -- just package-artifact=
  - new clean-consumer SwiftPM release-artifact smoke task
  - =mise exec -- just release-check= or documented expected release blockers
- Claude review plan: run a scoped plan consult after research, implement after
  feedback, then run a diff review and iterate once.

Implementation progress:

- Added =scripts/test-release-consumer-smoke.py=, a reusable clean-consumer
  harness that requires an HTTPS artifact URL and checksum, generates a
  temporary SwiftPM executable consumer outside the repo, forces
  =ECRITUM_RELEASE_RUNTIME_REQUIRED=1=, verifies Ecritum's release-mode manifest
  selects the remote =EcritumRuntime= binary target, rejects stale local release
  zip/checksum/manifest evidence, builds with isolated SwiftPM =HOME=, =TMPDIR=,
  and build paths, confirms SwiftPM downloaded =EcritumRuntime.framework= under
  the build directory instead of using =dist/local=, runs the executable with an
  empty =PATH=, and checks linked Mach-O paths for GraalVM/JDK/native-build
  leaks.
- Added a manifest-only script mode for cheap release-manifest validation tests;
  the full clean-consumer smoke still requires a positive HTTPS artifact
  download, build, and runtime execution.
- Added SwiftPM =workspace-state.json= validation after build: exactly one
  =EcritumRuntime= artifact for package identity =ecritum=, remote source type
  reported by SwiftPM, artifact path under the isolated SwiftPM build
  directory, no =dist/local= fallback, and the expected macOS framework slice.
- Added =just test-release-consumer-smoke= with optional URL/checksum
  arguments and environment fallback.
- Tightened =release-check.sh= so =ECRITUM_CONSUMER_ARTIFACT_CHECKSUM= without
  =ECRITUM_CONSUMER_ARTIFACT_URL= fails explicitly instead of entering the smoke
  with an incomplete hosted-artifact configuration.
- Added negative release-tool tests for non-HTTPS artifact URLs, invalid
  checksum shape, stale local release zip detection, and release-manifest
  target selection, checksum sidecar mismatch, package-manifest checksum
  mismatch, and =workspace-state.json= local/missing/duplicate/missing-source
  artifact shapes.
- Relaxed release-manifest validation to accept SwiftPM's real
  =remote/archive/<url-basename>.zip= path while still requiring a remote
  single-component zip archive path. This fixed the positive hosted run where
  SwiftPM resolved the Catbox artifact as =remote/archive/nr0ybn.zip=.
- Integrated optional clean-consumer evidence into =release-check.sh=:
  =build/release/clean-consumer.json= records either the positive HTTPS
  consumer result or a skipped gate explaining that SwiftPM binary target URLs
  require HTTPS and no artifact URL was supplied.
- Updated =docs/release-gates.md= with the HTTPS requirement, command example,
  and exact validation behavior.

Review evidence:

- Tests, Release, Swift DX, and Security/Unix personas all agreed that the
  existing =MacSmokeApp= path-dependency smoke does not prove M7-002. They
  required a generated external consumer, release-required manifest mode,
  no-local-fallback assertions, isolated build/runtime environments, stale
  artifact protection, and clear diagnostics.
- Local spike showed SwiftPM rejects =http://127.0.0.1= binary target URLs with
  =invalid URL scheme for binary target 'EcritumRuntime'; valid schemes are:
  'https'=, so M7-002 cannot honestly use a loopback HTTP server as acceptance
  evidence.
- Local loopback HTTPS with =SSL_CERT_FILE= and =REQUESTS_CA_BUNDLE= reached the
  artifact download path, but SwiftPM still rejected the self-signed certificate
  via macOS trust evaluation. A temporary-keychain spike was abandoned after
  Release/Security review because locally trusted loopback HTTPS would be
  development evidence only, not clean release evidence.
- Release/Security reviewer decision: M7-002 DONE requires a real hosted HTTPS
  artifact URL and matching checksum. If temporary loopback HTTPS is ever added
  as a developer convenience, it must use a disposable keychain, restore the
  original keychain search list on every exit path, delete all cert/key/keychain
  temp files, bind only to loopback, kill the server, and fail closed if cleanup
  cannot be verified.
- Claude plan consult recommended requiring caller-provided HTTPS URL/checksum
  instead of self-signed local HTTPS or =file://= workarounds. It also called out
  local-path masking, artifact provenance assertions, and the boundary between
  M7-002 validation plumbing and later public hosting/signing automation.
- Claude diff review after the workspace-state iteration completed successfully.
  Findings acted on: tighten =release-check.sh= partial env handling, require
  =source.type == "remote"= instead of allowing a missing source type, add
  sidecar/manifest/missing-state/missing-source tests, and make missing Mach-O
  file diagnostics explicit before =otool=.
- Claude findings accepted without code change: the =DYLD_*= isolation concern
  does not apply because the runtime subprocess receives an explicit three-key
  environment instead of inheriting the parent environment; the justfile uses
  positional task parameters intentionally and converts them to script flags.
- 2026-06-06 Claude diff review for the hosted-basename fix returned no
  blockers. Non-blocking feedback to require a single zip basename under
  =remote/archive/= was implemented with a fake-Swift regression test.
- Tests/Security/Unix and Release/Swift DX post-change reviewers confirmed the
  acceptance bar: M7-002 requires =clean-consumer.json= with =ok: true= from a
  real trusted HTTPS URL, not self-signed loopback or local-path evidence.

Verification evidence:

** DONE Milestone M8: Release Candidate Closure

Goal: close the remaining product blockers before Ecritum can be treated as a
release candidate rather than a local Full candidate.

Lead: Engineering Manager.
Required reviewers: Architecture, Release, Security, Tests, Swift DX, Unix.

Definition of done:

- Active debt ledger is empty or each remaining entry has an accepted
  owner-approved deferral outside the release claim.
- Public diagnostic stack-frame behavior is either implemented through the C ABI
  or explicitly dropped from the support claim.
- A publishable release lane is selected and passes its gates with no hidden
  local path, signing, license, or hosting dependency.
- First public release artifacts use the Community release tier: hosted over
  HTTPS, checksummed for SwiftPM, verified by a clean SwiftPM consumer, and
  documented as not Developer ID signed, notarized, or stapled.
- Trusted macOS release artifacts remain an optional later tier requiring
  Developer ID signing, notarization, and stapling evidence or an accepted
  archive exception.

*** DONE M8-001 Decide public diagnostic stack-frame ABI

Lead persona: Architecture.
Reviewer personas: Swift DX, Tests, Security.
Debt: ECRITUM-DEBT-0007.

Definition of done:

- ADR/update chooses one path: implement a stable redacted stack-frame ABI, or
  drop stack-frame diagnostics from v0 support claims.
- If implemented, `docs/abi/ecritum-c-abi.json`, `ecritum.h`, wrapper code,
  backend result format, Swift `EcritumErrorDetails.stack`, and ABI checker
  coverage are updated together.
- Artifact-backed C/Swift/conformance tests prove source-name plus stack-frame
  behavior where supported.

Verification plan:

- `mise exec -- just check-abi`
- `mise exec -- just test-c-abi-eval`
- `mise exec -- just test-swift`
- `mise exec -- just test-xcframework-eval-smoke`
- `mise exec -- just conformance`

Decision:

- Accepted ADR-024. Ecritum v0 does not claim public diagnostic stack-frame,
  line, or column support through the C ABI.
- The v0 native diagnostic surface remains status, category, redacted message,
  operation, language, and host-supplied source name.
- Swift keeps `EcritumStackFrame` and `EcritumErrorDetails.stack` as a
  future-compatible API shape, but native-backed v0 diagnostics leave the stack
  empty unless a later ABI adds frame accessors.
- No public C symbol, manifest entry, wrapper implementation, or runtime
  behavior changed.

Review:

- Architecture reviewer recommended explicitly dropping stack-frame diagnostics
  from v0 support claims because the safe v0 C ABI already covers status,
  category, message, operation, language, and source name, while frames need
  cross-runtime redaction, limits, source-location trust rules, and capability
  detection. Implemented.
- Swift DX/TDD reviewer independently recommended the same deferral because the
  C ABI, ABI ledger, backend codec, wrapper records, Swift copy path, and
  conformance tests only support status/category/message/operation/language/
  source-name today. Implemented.
- Claude plan review: direct `claude -p` attempt timed out after 90 seconds
  with no output (`CLAUDE_STATUS=124`). Persona reviews were used as fallback.

Verification:

- `mise exec -- just plan-check` -> exit 0.
- `mise exec -- just check-abi` -> exit 0.
- `mise exec -- just test-c-abi-eval` -> exit 0.
- `mise exec -- just conformance` -> exit 0, 23 tests passed plus scaffold
  provider JSON generation.
- `mise exec -- just test-swift` -> exit 0, 65 tests passed.
- `mise exec -- just test-xcframework-eval-smoke` -> exit 0, 65 tests passed.
- `mise exec -- just test-swift-scaffold` -> exit 0, 65 tests passed with
  expected artifact-backed skips.
- Support-claim scan removed stale v0 line/column and stack-frame claims from
  ADR-002, ADR-005, ADR-016, and ADR-021.

*** DONE M8-002 Produce true Core artifact or rebaseline ADR-018

Lead persona: Release.
Reviewer personas: GraalVM Runtime, Architecture, Tests, Security.

Definition of done:

Decision:

- Implemented a true SCI/Clojure-only Core artifact lane and kept the combined
  SCI/GraalJS/Lua artifact as explicit Full.
- ADR-018 now accepts the measured SCI-only Core baseline because the original
  M1 Core size tripwires were below a real embedded SCI runtime.
- Core remains the default release lane. Full must be selected explicitly and
  cannot be selected through ambient `ECRITUM_RELEASE_LANE`.

Implementation:

- Added Maven `core` and `full` source profiles. Shared SCI/value/stdlib support
  remains in `native/src/main/java/ecritum`.
- Moved Core private entrypoints to `native/src/core/java/ecritum`.
- Moved Full private entrypoints plus JavaScript and Lua adapters/tests to
  `native/src/full/...`.
- `native-core` builds with `-Pnative,core` and exports only Clojure private
  entrypoints.
- `native-full` builds with `-Pnative,full`, exports Clojure, JavaScript, and
  Lua private entrypoints, and still refreshes the legacy `build/native` path.
- The C wrapper now compiles with Core language guards and has a C contract test
  proving JavaScript/Lua eval start returns runtime-unavailable for Core.
- `xcframework-core` and `xcframework-full` write lane metadata into
  `Resources/ecritum-runtime-lane.json`.
- Package, size, dependency-delta, SBOM, and release-check tools validate and
  propagate selected lanes.
- Clojure native conformance provider accepts `ECRITUM_NATIVE_FRAMEWORK` so Core
  and Full artifacts can be tested without swapping `dist/local`.

- Core artifact budget: 35,000,000 bytes.

- Core private runtime baseline: 30,511,744 bytes.
- Core wrapper baseline: 147,280 bytes.

*** DONE M8-004 Public release signing and notarization gate

Lead persona: Release.
Reviewer personas: Security, Swift DX, Tests, Unix.

  runtime options for every shipped slice and nested dylib.

- Post-unpack `codesign --verify --deep --strict` equivalent passes.
- Hosted HTTPS URL/checksum SwiftPM resolution is required for public release;
  local `.binaryTarget(path:)` cannot satisfy the gate.
- ECRITUM-DEBT-0012 is resolved.

  skipped for contributor builds.

*** DONE M8-005 Adopt GitHub-hosted Community release path

Lead persona: Release.
Reviewer personas: Security, Swift DX, Tests, Unix.

Definition of done:

- ADR-010 distinguishes Community release from optional Trusted macOS release.
- Community release requires GitHub Releases or equivalent immutable HTTPS
  hosting, a SwiftPM checksum, clean SwiftPM consumer validation, package
  reproducibility, ABI, size, SBOM, license, dependency-delta, vulnerability,
  and artifact-inspection gates.
- Community release records explicit skipped signing evidence saying the
  artifact does not claim Developer ID signing, notarization, or stapling.
- `release-check-community` fails if hosted SwiftPM consumer validation would be
  skipped.
- `release-check-public` remains available for the later Trusted macOS tier and
  still requires Developer ID/notary/stapling evidence.
- Security intake is user-owned and accepted by owner attestation on
  2026-06-07; the project still documents GitHub private vulnerability
  reporting as the intended intake path.

  ECRITUM_CONSUMER_ARTIFACT_CHECKSUM=...
  mise exec -- just release-check-community core`

  Releases URL, not `/latest/`.

  signed, notarized, or stapled.

  design. The Community release gate records this as an explicit skipped public

** DONE Milestone M9: Product and Architecture Reset for the Default Full Runtime

Goal: reset the product and architecture contract for the next release. Ecritum
will have one default runtime artifact, not public Core and Full artifacts. That
default artifact must ultimately contain Clojure/SCI, GraalJS, LuaJ, GraalPy,
and TruffleRuby, and remain consumable as a normal SwiftPM dependency.

Lead: Engineering Manager.
Required reviewers: Architecture, GraalVM Runtime, Release, Swift DX, Security,
Tests/TDD, Unix, Clean Code, Technical Debt.

Accepted product scope:

- One default runtime artifact for the next release; no separate public Core and
  Full artifacts.
- macOS arm64 remains the first supported platform slice.
- Python and Ruby package support is intentionally minimal: only the language
  runtime and standard/runtime resources required by Ecritum itself. No `pip`,
  gems, third-party package directories, package downloads, package installs,
  native extensions, native wheels, C extensions, `ctypes`, `cffi`, FFI/NFI, or
  mutable package caches in this release.
- Default policy remains deny-by-default for filesystem, network, process,
  environment, reflection/class loading, direct Java access, raw Polyglot access,
  native library loading, native access, and host access outside registered
  Ecritum capabilities.
- Docs, tutorials, examples, release notes, measured artifact/app-size impact,
  cold start, first eval per language, and idle RSS are release blockers.

Roadmap sequencing:

- M9 resets ADRs and public support claims.
- M10 fixes normal SwiftPM distribution and promotes the existing Clojure,
  JavaScript, and Lua runtime lane to the default artifact path.
- M11 adds GraalPy behind feasibility, resource, security, conformance, and
  measurement gates.
- M12 adds TruffleRuby behind version-coordinate, resource, security,
  conformance, and measurement gates.
- M13 expands docs, tutorials, examples, and measured reference metrics.
- M14 publishes the next Community release only after the hosted no-env
  consumer, packaged app, license/SBOM, and five-language gates pass.

Milestone definition of done:

- ADR-008, ADR-009, ADR-010, ADR-018, and ADR-023 are updated or superseded
  before runtime implementation changes.
- README, docs, release gates, and support claims no longer describe Core as the
  next-release default artifact. Historical v0.1.0 release notes remain factual.
- Python/Ruby package limits, accepted performance budgets, and the SwiftPM
  distribution strategy are recorded in accepted ADR text.
- `PROJECT.org` contains milestone tasks with owners, reviewers, DoD, and
  verification plans for M10-M14.
- DEBT.md remains empty or records any accepted deferral with owner, expiry,
  exit condition, removal task, and verification.

Persona debate and review record:

- Architecture/GraalVM Runtime sub-agent `019ea7e8-c106-74d1-9101-e30ff90b365a`
  recommended splitting the work into M9-M14, updating/superseding ADR-008,
  ADR-009, ADR-010, ADR-018, and ADR-023, and treating Ruby version skew as the
  highest runtime risk.
- Release/Swift DX sub-agent `019ea7e8-df56-7302-9940-b7c483b87c06` recommended
  making `Package.swift` default to a checked-in GitHub Release URL/checksum
  when `dist/local` is absent, keeping env URL overrides only for staging/tests,
  and not using `native/pom.xml` as a contributor sentinel because SwiftPM
  consumers clone the repo and would also have it.
- Security/TDD sub-agent `019ea7e8-fdbf-7762-8c5e-2753484dc650` required that no
  language be documented as supported until strict conformance and strict abuse
  suites have zero required pending cases for that language.
- Claude plan challenge: direct `claude -p` attempt on the initial roadmap timed
  out after 90 seconds with no output (`CLAUDE_STATUS=124`); persona reviews are
  recorded as the fallback.
- Claude review on the refined M9-M14 roadmap completed with findings on
  feasibility exits, task dependencies, M10 URL/version strategy, and M14
  five-language hosted verification. EM accepted the dependency and verification
  fixes. EM rejected an automatic N-1 language release fallback because the user
  requirement for this project is all five languages; any scope reduction must be
  an explicit ADR and user-approved project change.

Milestone verification plan:

- `mise exec -- just plan-check`
- ADR support-claim scan for Core/Full default language.
- Claude review on the ADR diff, or timeout recorded.
- Persona review from Architecture, Release, Security, Tests/TDD, Unix, Clean
  Code, and Technical Debt.

Milestone completion evidence:

- M9-000, M9-001, and M9-002 are DONE.
- ADR-025 accepted the single-default-runtime-artifact policy.
- ADR-008, ADR-009, ADR-010, ADR-018, and ADR-023 now carry ADR-025
  supersession notes for next-release artifact policy.
- Active docs and PLAN now distinguish historical v0.1.0/M8 Core/Full behavior
  from the next-release single default artifact policy.
- Active release-facing Core/Full implementation cleanup is tracked as
  ECRITUM-DEBT-0013 and assigned to M10.
- `mise exec -- just plan-check` -> PASS.
- `mise exec -- just test` -> PASS.
- Existing hosted community release gate with v0.1.0 URL/checksum ->
  `mise exec -- just release-check-community core` PASS.
- Current no-env community release gate remains a known M10 blocker.

*** DONE M9-001 Adopt the single default artifact policy

Lead persona: Architecture Expert Engineer.
Reviewer personas: GraalVM Runtime, Release, Security, Tests/TDD, Technical Debt.
Active review agents: Architecture `019ea7f7-4723-7812-92a3-95744c5a780d`;
Release/SwiftPM `019ea7f7-4a48-7931-9e9f-58752e924526`; Security/TDD
`019ea7f7-4da0-7083-9d17-cd1fa7610141`.

Definition of done:

- Accepted ADR text records that the next release has one default artifact that
  contains Clojure, JavaScript, Lua, Python, and Ruby once all runtime gates pass.
- ADR-008 and ADR-009 are superseded or amended so Python/Ruby are no longer
  described as future Full-only candidates, while preserving the no-package and
  no-native-extension limits.
- ADR-010 records the default remote SwiftPM binary-target strategy.
- ADR-018 records single-artifact size/performance budgets from measurements
  rather than Core-vs-Full deltas.
- ADR-023 records Lua promotion rules under the single default artifact.
- DEBT.md records any accepted policy mismatch that remains after ADR updates.

Verification plan:

- `mise exec -- just plan-check`
- `mise exec -- just test`
- `mise exec -- just release-check-community`
- `rg -n "Core is the default|Full is explicit|Full-only|Core/Full" README.md
  docs PROJECT.org PLAN.org`
- Claude plan review on the ADR diff, or timeout recorded.
- Persona review from Architecture, Release, Security, and Tests/TDD.

Progress and evidence:

- Added ADR-025 as the accepted single-default-runtime-artifact policy.
- Added supersession notes to ADR-008, ADR-009, ADR-010, ADR-018, and ADR-023.
- Added ADR-025 to the ADR backlog.
- Architecture review `019ea7f7-4723-7812-92a3-95744c5a780d` accepted the
  superseding-ADR approach and required explicit ABI/layout language; added.
- Release/SwiftPM review `019ea7f7-4a48-7931-9e9f-58752e924526` required

  zero-required-pending strict conformance/abuse before support claims and
  explicit Python/Ruby package/native-extension denials; added.
- `mise exec -- just plan-check` -> PASS.

  FAIL in current M8 implementation; confirms the M10 distribution blocker.

  mise exec -- just release-check-community core` -> PASS.

  seconds with no output (`CLAUDE_STATUS=124`).

** DONE Milestone M10: Default SwiftPM Distribution and Existing Runtime Promotion

Goal: make the current Clojure/SCI, GraalJS, and LuaJ runtime lane the normal
SwiftPM artifact path before adding Python or Ruby. A clean SwiftPM app must be
able to depend on a tagged Ecritum release without Ecritum-specific environment
variables and receive `EcritumRuntime.framework` automatically.

Lead persona: Release, Licensing, and Distribution Engineer.
Reviewer personas: Swift DX, Unix, Tests/TDD, Architecture, Security.
Depends on: M9.

Definition of done:

- `Package.swift` defaults to a checked-in GitHub Release URL and SwiftPM
  checksum when `dist/local/EcritumRuntime.xcframework` is absent.
- The next version and staged/final release URL strategy are selected before the
  checked-in default URL is changed. A draft or prerelease validation URL may be
  used only if M14 replaces or confirms it before publication.
- `ECRITUM_RUNTIME_URL` and `ECRITUM_RUNTIME_CHECKSUM` remain only for release
  staging/tests and still must be provided together.
- Local contributor flows still work through `dist/local` and scaffold/no-runtime
  test mode.
- No contributor sentinel relies on `native/pom.xml`, because external SwiftPM
  consumers clone the repo and would also have it.
- Clean no-env SwiftPM consumers run Clojure, JavaScript, and Lua from the
  default artifact.
- Packaged `.app` smoke embeds `EcritumRuntime.framework` and generates no
  intentional crash reports.

Verification plan:

- `swift package describe --type json` in the repo with no Ecritum env vars.
- Clean external SwiftPM consumer from a GitHub tag with no `dist/`, temporary
  HOME/cache, and no Ecritum env vars.
- `mise exec -- just test-swift-scaffold`
- `mise exec -- just test-swift`
- `mise exec -- just examples`
- `mise exec -- just packaged-app-smoke`
- `mise exec -- just release-check-community`
- Negative: setting only URL or checksum fails clearly.

*** DONE M10-001 Add default remote runtime manifest behavior

Lead persona: Release, Licensing, and Distribution Engineer.
Reviewer personas: Swift DX, Unix, Tests/TDD.
Active review agents: Release/SwiftPM `019ea807-c261-7772-8c44-facb881dff1a`;
Tests/TDD `019ea807-c531-7fc3-a912-7e9384e6bd62`.

Definition of done:

- Next version, tag naming, staged artifact URL, and final hosted URL replacement
  rules are recorded before changing `Package.swift`.
- `Package.swift` selects the local artifact first, otherwise the checked-in
  release URL/checksum, otherwise scaffold mode only when explicitly intended by
  tests.
- Tests cover local artifact, default remote, explicit env override, missing
  checksum, missing URL, and scaffold/no-runtime mode.
- The implementation is deterministic under clean SwiftPM package resolution.

Verification plan:

- `python3 -B -m unittest Tests/Release/test_package_artifact.py`
- `mise exec -- just test-swift-scaffold`
- `swift package describe --type json` with no Ecritum env vars.
- Clean no-env consumer smoke.

Progress and evidence:

- Updated `Package.swift` to use deterministic manifest selection:
  local `dist/local` first for contributors, paired env URL/checksum as a
  staging override when local is absent, checked-in hosted URL/checksum as the
  default remote fallback, and explicit scaffold mode only when
  `ECRITUM_LOCAL_RUNTIME=0`.
- `ECRITUM_RELEASE_RUNTIME_REQUIRED=1` now ignores local artifacts and uses the
  paired env override when present, otherwise the checked-in default remote.
- `ECRITUM_LOCAL_RUNTIME=0` now fails clearly if combined with
  `ECRITUM_RELEASE_RUNTIME_REQUIRED` or runtime URL/checksum env vars.
- Added fixture-based release tests for local/default/env/release-required/
  scaffold precedence, partial env failures, `native/pom.xml` non-sentinel
  behavior, default URL/checksum shape, and no-env default-manifest smoke mode.
- Added `--use-default-package-runtime` to `scripts/test-release-consumer-smoke.py`
  so release tests can validate the checked-in manifest default without injecting
  Ecritum runtime env vars.
- Recorded `ECRITUM-DEBT-0014`: the checked-in default URL currently points to
  the existing hosted v0.1.0 Community Core artifact as a live bootstrap. M14
  must replace it with the next release's single default artifact URL/checksum.
- Release/SwiftPM review `019ea807-c261-7772-8c44-facb881dff1a` completed; its
  precedence and temporary-URL concerns were incorporated or recorded as debt.
- Tests/TDD review `019ea807-c531-7fc3-a912-7e9384e6bd62` completed with Claude
  agreement; its matrix and no-env smoke recommendations were incorporated.
- `python3 -B -m unittest Tests/Release/test_package_artifact.py` -> PASS, 43
  tests.
- `mise exec -- just test-release-tools` -> PASS, 107 tests.
- `mise exec -- just test-swift-scaffold` -> PASS.
- `mise exec -- just test-swift` -> PASS.
- `ECRITUM_RELEASE_RUNTIME_REQUIRED=1 swift package describe --type json` ->
  resolves `EcritumRuntime` as `remote/archive/EcritumRuntime.xcframework.zip`.
- `ECRITUM_LOCAL_RUNTIME=0 ECRITUM_RELEASE_RUNTIME_REQUIRED=1 swift package
  describe --type json` -> expected FAIL with explicit conflict message.
- Direct Claude implementation diff review attempted with `claude -p`; timed out
  after 90 seconds with no output (`CLAUDE_STATUS=124`).

*** DONE M10-002 Collapse release-facing Core/Full lane behavior

Lead persona: Release, Licensing, and Distribution Engineer.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Technical Debt, Tests/TDD.
Depends on: M9-001, M9-002.
Active review agents: Release `019ea813-0dec-7071-94c5-04c004fbbfc6`;
Technical Debt `019ea813-107d-70d1-ab08-7e88e7acda56`; TDD/Unix
`019ea813-148b-7063-9c28-62bec3848eb7`.

Definition of done:

- Release-facing tasks package the single default artifact by default.
- Any remaining `core`/`full` implementation names are internal, documented, and
  not visible as product artifacts.
- `release-check` and `release-check-community` validate the artifact they will
  publish rather than a stale local lane.
- Package manifests record included runtimes and resource inventory.

Verification plan:

- `mise exec -- just test-release-tools`
- `mise exec -- just release-check-community`
- `mise exec -- just package-artifact`
- `mise exec -- just package-artifact-verify`
- `mise exec -- just inspect`

Progress and evidence:

- Collapsed release-facing `just` recipes so `release-check`,
  `release-check-community`, `release-check-public`, `package-artifact`,
  `package-artifact-verify`, `size`, `license-report`, `sbom`,
  `license-report-strict`, `third-party-notices`, and `check-dep-delta` operate
  on the single default artifact without a public lane argument.
- Updated `release-check.sh` to reject `--lane`, write unscoped release
  evidence under `build/release`, package
  `dist/release/EcritumRuntime.xcframework.zip`, and let community mode validate
  the checked-in Package.swift default remote target without requiring
  `ECRITUM_CONSUMER_ARTIFACT_URL`.
- Updated `package-artifact.py` manifests to record `artifactKind: default`,
  `implementationProfile`, `includedRuntimes`, `resourceInventory`, checksums,
  slices, files, and normalized timestamp. Legacy `releaseLane=full` framework
  metadata is accepted as a transitional internal profile; legacy
  `releaseLane=core` is rejected for default release packaging.
- Updated `build-xcframework.sh` to write `Resources/ecritum-runtime.json` with
  artifact kind, implementation profile, and included runtimes. The old `--lane`
  flag is retired in favor of internal `--implementation-profile`.
- Updated `test-release-consumer-smoke.py` so the default smoke is lane-free and
  proves Clojure, JavaScript, and Lua. `--use-default-package-runtime` now forces
  remote resolution through the checked-in default without staging URL/checksum
  env vars, even when `dist/local` exists in the contributor checkout.
- Updated size, license, SBOM, dependency-delta, public-signing, and inspection
  tooling/tests to use the default artifact contract.
- Updated `docs/release-gates.md` and
  `docs/performance-and-artifact-budgets.md` to remove active public lane
  commands and document lane-free release paths.
- Resolved `ECRITUM-DEBT-0013`. The final hosted no-env clean SwiftPM consumer
  that runs Clojure, JavaScript, and Lua remains assigned to M10-003 and
  `ECRITUM-DEBT-0014`.
- Release review `019ea813-0dec-7071-94c5-04c004fbbfc6` completed; it
  recommended one public `default` artifact and keeping Core/Full only as
  internal profiles. Implemented.
- Technical Debt review `019ea813-107d-70d1-ab08-7e88e7acda56` completed; it
  required removal of public lane recipes, lane-driven release-check behavior,
  and release-lane package metadata. Implemented and debt ledger updated.
- TDD/Unix review `019ea813-148b-7063-9c28-62bec3848eb7` completed; it required
  retired-lane tests, unscoped release paths, runtime/resource inventory, and
  lane-free Clojure/JavaScript/Lua smoke. Implemented.
- Claude plan review completed successfully and identified the same critical
  gaps: community default manifest behavior, runtime metadata migration, Lua in
  release consumer smoke, default size budgets, dependency/license lane removal,
  and stale support-claim scan. Implemented.
- Direct Claude post-change diff review was attempted with `claude -p`, but it
  hung for several minutes and was terminated (`CLAUDE_STATUS=143`). EM accepted
  the completed persona reviews and passing release gates as the fallback.

`019ea834-6e4c-7211-9a21-7b6e67ac5c35`.

- A fresh external SwiftPM executable package depending on the tag imports
  Ecritum, builds from an empty cache, reports `runtimeArtifactAvailable == true`,
  and evaluates Clojure, JavaScript, and Lua.
- A packaged macOS `.app` embeds the framework, runs without DYLD overrides, and
  has stable install names/rpaths.
- The smoke app no longer uses intentional missing-framework launches as a
  negative test.

- `mise exec -- just packaged-app-smoke`

  `scripts/test-packaged-app-smoke.sh` so the packaged `.app` evaluates
  Clojure, JavaScript, and Lua from the embedded framework, runs with an empty
  command `PATH` and no `DYLD_*` overrides, records link/rpath evidence, and
  fails if a new `EcritumSmokeApp` crash report appears.
- M10-003B hosted no-env SwiftPM proof: after an explicit release-operation
  approval to push/tag/upload, replace the bootstrap default URL/checksum,
  verify a fresh external SwiftPM consumer from the GitHub tag with no Ecritum
  env vars and empty caches, and close `ECRITUM-DEBT-0014`.

- `Examples/MacSmokeApp` creates a runtime with `.clojure`, `.javascript`, and
  `.lua`, checks `Ecritum.runtimeArtifactAvailable`, registers one host callback,
  evaluates all three languages through the public Swift API, and prints
  `EcritumSmokeApp version=0.1.0 clojure=42 javascript=42 lua=42`.
- `scripts/test-packaged-app-smoke.sh` copies the packaged framework into
  `Contents/Frameworks`, signs ad hoc when `codesign` exists, runs the copied
  app from a temporary directory with `env -i`, empty command `PATH`, and no
  `DYLD_*` variables, then verifies install names/rpaths and rejects workspace,
  GraalVM, JDK, native-target, or build-native paths.
- The script counts `EcritumSmokeApp` crash reports before and after the run and
  fails if the count increases.
- No hosted release artifact or GitHub tag is created without explicit user
  approval to push/upload.

- Added `Tests/Release/test_packaged_app_smoke.py` to protect the packaged-app

** DONE Milestone M11: GraalPy Runtime Support

Goal: add Python through GraalPy without external Python installs, package
managers, third-party packages, or native extensions.

Lead persona: GraalVM and Polyglot Runtime Engineer.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Security, Tests/TDD, Release, Clean Code.
Depends on: M9, M10.

Definition of done:

- Current GraalPy embedding, resource, licensing, and Native Image guidance is
  reviewed and cited in task notes or an ADR update.
- Maven coordinates are pinned to the repo GraalVM line, or an ADR accepts tested
  version skew.
- Python is available through the public C ABI and Swift API with the same
  lifecycle, value, host-function, and error semantics as other languages.
- Python imports of `java`, raw `polyglot`, `ctypes`, `cffi`, `socket`,
  `subprocess`, environment access, unrestricted filesystem access, and native
  extensions fail clearly.
- Python strict conformance and strict abuse suites have zero required pending
  cases before docs claim support.
- Size, cold start, first Python eval, idle RSS, dependency delta, license/SBOM,
  and resource inventory evidence is recorded.
- If M11-001 cannot prove GraalPy feasibility in one focused spike change, the
  EM marks M11 blocked, records logs and upstream references, writes or updates
  an ADR with options, and asks the user before changing the five-language
  release requirement.

Verification plan:

- Focused Java GraalPy evaluator/resource tests.
- `mise exec -- just native`
- `mise exec -- just xcframework`
- `mise exec -- just conformance-python-native`
- `mise exec -- just security-python`
- `mise exec -- just check-security-static`
- `mise exec -- just test-swift`
- `mise exec -- just check-abi`
- Python first-eval, size, RSS, license, dependency, and package-resource
  evidence recorded in PROJECT.org.

Completion evidence, 2026-06-08:

- M11-001 proved GraalPy coordinates, Native Image resources, licensing, and
  local artifact feasibility.
- M11-002 wired Python into the C ABI, Swift API, values, errors, host
  callbacks, metadata, examples, and local artifact path without claiming
  hosted public support early.
- M11-003 closed the public-support gates for the local full artifact:
  deny-by-default GraalVM permissions, Ecritum-owned Python sandbox prelude,
  Python timeout propagation, strict Python conformance/security providers,
  Python release metrics, SBOM/license/dependency updates, and release-package
  verification.
- Final verification:
  - `mise exec -- just test` -> PASS.
  - `mise exec -- just release-check` -> PASS.
  - `claude -p` post-implementation review -> PASS, no blockers.
  - Python strict conformance -> PASS, 14 passed / 0 failed / 0 pending.
  - Python strict abuse suite -> PASS, 68 passed / 0 failed / 0 pending.
  - Release zip checksum -> `d07b5c2715d1f8933dad12f7903580003528cbd164717bf7db4b1520c0b172aa`.
  - Release artifact includes `clojure`, `javascript`, `lua`, and `python`.
  - Size gate -> PASS: artifact 365,383,882 bytes, private runtime
    364,748,512 bytes, wrapper 147,648 bytes.
  - Python first eval -> PASS: p50 43.843 ms, p95 53.703 ms.
  - Python post-eval RSS -> PASS: p50 216,694,784 bytes, p95
    224,477,184 bytes.
- `ECRITUM-DEBT-0015` moved to resolved debt. The lexical Python guard is now
  defense in depth rather than the only enforcement mechanism.
- Public hosted SwiftPM docs/defaults remain gated to M14 because public hosted
  consumers still need a published Python-capable artifact URL and checksum.

*** DONE M11-001 Prove GraalPy coordinates, resources, and Native Image build

Lead persona: GraalVM and Polyglot Runtime Engineer.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Release, Security.

Active EM note, 2026-06-08:

- Status: active feasibility spike for the next implementation slice.
- Integration lane: current clean `jj` workspace. No `.workspaces/` or
  `workspaces/` convention exists, so the EM is not creating a parallel
  workspace without a project directory choice.
- Active agents:
  - Gibbs (`019ea88e-f7cf-7153-ac37-3b33d23d5479`): GraalVM/Polyglot Runtime,
    read-only research on Maven coordinates, resource layout, and Native Image
    requirements.
  - Curie (`019ea88e-fab7-7a73-8ba1-82cf472147bb`): Architecture/Security,
    read-only review of denial boundaries, ABI impact, and ADR requirements.
  - Pascal (`019ea88e-fef6-7332-be9b-b0d967c98949`): TDD/Verification/Release,
    read-only review of red-green tests, release gates, and evidence format.
- Current upstream references reviewed:
  - Oracle GraalVM 25 embedding guide says language dependencies are available
    from Maven Central under `org.graalvm.polyglot`, language artifacts require
    `<type>pom</type>`, and community-licensed variants use the `-community`
    suffix.
  - Oracle GraalVM 25 embedding guide says Native Image can include language
    resources by default, copy them with `-H:+CopyLanguageResources`, and look
    them up relative to the executable/shared library or via
    `-Dpolyglot.engine.resourcePath`.
  - GraalPy embedding build-tools docs say `graalpy-maven-plugin` manages
    Python application files, third-party packages, and the Python standard
    library, and can deploy resources either as Java resources/VFS or an
    external directory.
  - Maven Central for `org.graalvm.python:python:25.0.2` shows runtime
    dependencies on `python-language`, `python-resources`, and
    `truffle-runtime`, with UPL, MIT, and PSF license declarations.
- Accepted initial plan:
  - Run a Claude plan review before implementation.
  - Use TDD for the first JVM-level Python eval proof: add a focused test first,
    observe the missing-runtime or missing-class failure, then add the minimal
    dependency/evaluator code needed to pass on the JVM.
  - Keep the C ABI and Swift API unchanged in M11-001 unless the Native Image
    proof reaches a point where an export is needed; public Python support waits
    for M11-002 and M11-003.
  - Use `org.graalvm.polyglot:python:${graalvm.version}` for the probe. The
    `python-community` coordinate resolves, but its POM marks it deprecated and
    says to use `org.graalvm.polyglot:python`.
  - Do not configure `graalpy-maven-plugin` package installation, third-party
    packages, `venv`, package-manager execution, or native-extension support in
    M11-001.
  - Stop and mark blocked if the minimal JVM eval cannot be made deterministic,
    if Native Image cannot either embed or copy Python resources with a clear
    artifact strategy, or if denial probes require enabling host/native/process/
    environment/filesystem access.
- Verification for this slice:
  - Baseline: `mise exec -- just test-java`
  - Dependency evidence: `mise exec -- mvn -s .mvn/settings.xml -f native/pom.xml
    -Pfull dependency:tree -Dscope=runtime`
  - Focused red/green JVM Python test.
  - Native Image probe: `mise exec -- just native`
  - Artifact inspection: `mise exec -- just inspect`
  - Post-change Claude diff review and second review after fixes.

Definition of done:

- Dependency tree, resource layout, Native Image flags, and framework resource
  strategy are documented from local evidence.
- A minimal Python eval reaches Native Image or records a concrete blocker with
  logs and upstream references.
- A blocker outcome does not count as Python support. It blocks M11 until the EM

  lexical guard for risky Python surfaces.

  filesystem/dynamic-eval entry points.

  changing the public C ABI or Swift API.

  `just test-python-native-probe` as reusable probe tasks.

  tests cannot become an unscanned blind spot.
- Added a language-aware `SciEvalResult.ok(language, value)` factory and moved
  JavaScript, Lua, and Python success paths to it. This fixes the hidden
  success-result language field before Python reaches the public API slice.
- Updated ADR-008 with coordinate, dependency, license, resource, size, native
  build, and packaging evidence.
- Added `ECRITUM-DEBT-0015` because the temporary lexical Python guard is not
  acceptable for a public support claim. M11-003 must replace or justify it with
  strict packaged abuse evidence before Python is documented or released.

Definition of done:

- Python can be requested in Swift with `.python`, in C runtime configuration
  with `"python"`, and through the eval/job/value/error C ABI.
- Python supports scalar, array/list, object/map, nil/null, boolean, integer,
  double, string, and bytes where the public value model supports them.
- Python scripts can call registered host functions and receive host-returned
  values.
- Python structured script errors map to Ecritum status/category/message/
  operation/language/source-name without unsafe diagnostic leakage.
- Successful Python results do not get mislabeled as Clojure anywhere in the
  public C/Swift path. If the backend wire codec exposes success-language
  metadata, tests prove Python success payloads preserve `python`.

Completion note, 2026-06-08:

- Anscombe's security plan was implemented: Python has a strict native abuse
  provider, deny-by-default GraalVM permissions, a sandbox prelude that replaces
  dangerous builtins, timeout probes, filesystem root checks, invalid-handle
  checks, and bypass escalation rules.
- Boyle's release/TDD plan was implemented: `security-python`,
  `conformance-python-native`, `bench-python-first-eval`, `bench-python-rss`,
  release-check Python metric outputs, license/dependency gates, and release
  tool tests all include Python.
- Bacon's runtime plan was implemented: effective `executionTimeoutNanos`
  reaches the Python evaluator, GraalVM resource limits and a watchdog interrupt
  map long-running Python scripts to `timeout`, and post-timeout recovery is
  proved through native eval smoke.
- Claude plan review found two blockers before implementation: missing
  bypass-contingency policy and missing `security-python`. Both were fixed.
- Claude implementation review found no blockers. Non-blocking follow-ups:
  broaden explicit introspection abuse probes (`type.__subclasses__`,
  `object.__subclasses__`, `__class__.__mro__`, `globals`, `locals`, `vars`,
  `dir`), consider elapsed-time checking around watchdog wakeups, and enrich
  Python lexical deny patterns for earlier diagnostics. These are not M11
  blockers because the actual enforcement is the sandbox prelude plus GraalVM
  denial, and strict native security/conformance passed.

Definition of done:

- Python abuse probes cover direct Java, raw Polyglot, `ctypes`, `cffi`, socket,
  subprocess, env, package install/load, native extension, and filesystem denial.
- Python abuse probes also cover lexical-guard bypasses and additional risky
  standard-library surfaces: `os.popen`, `signal`, `platform`, `posix`, `ssl`,
  `urllib`, `pathlib`, `tempfile`, `getpass`, `pickle`, `marshal`, `importlib`,
  dynamic import/eval/compile, `sys.path` mutation, bytecode-cache writes, and
  imports from unapproved directories.
- Python timeout/resource-limit behavior is proved through the packaged native
  eval path.
- Python stdlib facade behavior has native conformance coverage before any
  stdlib support claim.
- Python metrics are captured in the release evidence format.
- License/SBOM and dependency-delta inventories include GraalPy and bundled
  resources.
- `ECRITUM-DEBT-0015` is either removed because a stronger enforcement mechanism
  and strict abuse suite replace the lexical guard, or explicitly re-accepted in
  an ADR with public-support consequences.
- Public docs, examples, release notes, and checked-in hosted SwiftPM artifact
  defaults still do not claim Python until M11-003 and the relevant M14 release
  gates pass.

Verification plan:

- `mise exec -- just security-python`

- `mise exec -- just bench-idle-rss`
