** DONE Milestone M12: TruffleRuby Runtime Support

Goal: add Ruby through TruffleRuby without external Ruby installs, RubyGems,
Bundler installs, third-party gems, native gems, C extensions, or NFI/FFI.

Lead persona: GraalVM and Polyglot Runtime Engineer.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Security, Tests/TDD, Release, Clean Code.
Depends on: M9, M10.

Definition of done:

- TruffleRuby Maven/version feasibility is resolved before implementation.
  The current candidate path is `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1`, not the
  old `org.graalvm.polyglot:ruby` line. The candidate must pass ADR-0027
  validation before public Ruby API work starts.
- Ruby is available through the public C ABI and Swift API with the same
  lifecycle, value, host-function, and error semantics as other languages.
- RubyGems, Bundler installation, runtime gem installation, native gems,
  C extensions, NFI/FFI, direct Java, raw Polyglot, subprocess, network,
  environment, and unrestricted filesystem access are blocked or disabled.
- Ruby strict conformance and strict abuse suites have zero required pending
  cases before docs claim support.
- Size, cold start, first Ruby eval, idle RSS, dependency delta, license/SBOM,
  and resource inventory evidence is recorded.
- If Ruby is blocked by feasibility, version alignment, security policy,
  release safety, or support-claim risk, the EM marks M12 blocked, records logs
  and upstream references, writes or updates an ADR with options, and asks the
  user before changing the five-language release requirement or accepting a
  self-use-only experimental path.

Active EM note, 2026-06-08:

- M11 is complete, so the team is starting M12 with the highest-risk task:
  TruffleRuby coordinate/resource feasibility.
- Active read-only review agents:
  - Herschel (`019ea917-92d0-7233-8315-41080d39a5ed`): GraalVM Runtime,
    verifying current TruffleRuby Maven coordinates and the smallest Native
    Image spike path.
  - Erdos (`019ea917-b5d1-7920-b595-165c44fb479f`): Release/Licensing,
    reviewing Ruby/LLVM dependency, resource, license, package, and metric
    evidence requirements.
  - Kant (`019ea917-d11e-7692-8b77-ee521d64187b`): Security/Architecture,
    reviewing Ruby escape surfaces, context options, and ADR requirements.
- EM local work: verify whether Ruby artifacts now exist for the repo GraalVM
  line (`25.0.2`), compare against the prior ADR-009 `25.0.0` finding, and use
  the result to decide whether M12-001 is an implementation spike or an ADR/user
  scope decision.
- EM decision after local evidence and first reviews: `25.0.2` Ruby artifacts
  are still unavailable, while `25.0.0` resolves. M12-001 may therefore proceed
  only as an isolated `ruby-probe` feasibility experiment under ADR-009. This is
  not a Ruby support claim, not a public ABI change, and not a release artifact
  dependency.

Active EM note, 2026-06-09:

- New upstream evidence changes the route but not the support gate.
- The old `org.graalvm.polyglot:ruby` Maven line still stops at `25.0.0`.
- Upstream TruffleRuby now publishes under `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby`; latest
  Maven release is `34.0.1`.
- `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1` depends on Truffle and LLVM `25.0.2`,
  which matches the repo's GraalVM line and avoids the old `25.0.0`
  cross-patch/downgrade problem rejected by ADR-0026.
- ADR-0027 is accepted as a conditional validation path. It does not claim Ruby
  support and does not unblock M12-002 by itself.
- M12 remains BLOCKED for public Ruby support, but not because the team cannot
  run Ruby. M12-001B has proven the new coordinates and Java-level probe path,
  and M12-001C has produced passing Native Image probe evidence ahead of its
  release-inventory dependency. The current blocker is release readiness:
  M12-004 must decide and tool the Ruby/LLVM license, SBOM, resource, package,
  vulnerability, and bundled-native-surface inventory before Ruby can move into
  the shipped public artifact path.
- Team review:
  - Herschel/GraalVM Runtime: keep M12 blocked; add a validation task for new
    coordinates, Polyglot registration, Native Image, option compatibility,
    resource lookup, no leakage, and security denials.
  - Kant/Architecture-Security: amend rather than erase ADR-0026; old
    `org.graalvm` blocker is obsolete, but release safety, RubyGems/Bundler,
    NFI/FFI/native, cache/resource immutability, load-path, Java/Polyglot escape,
    and strict abuse gates remain blockers.
  - Ramanujan/Release-TDD: sequence coordinate proof, license/SBOM/resource
    inventory, then Native Image release-shape probe before unblocking M12-002.
  - Claude plan review: plan is structurally sound if it includes local Maven
    resolution proof, Polyglot registration proof, license checks, independent
    TruffleRuby security-cadence tracking, and conditional ADR wording.
  - Claude post-change review: found stale M12-002 blocker metadata, missing
    M12-003 blocker text, and missing ownership for retiring/replacing the old
    `25.0.0` probe. Fixed by updating M12-002 dependencies, adding explicit
    M12-003 blocker text, and creating M12-001D.
  - Claude second review: no remaining blockers or unsafe Ruby support claims;
    requested consistency by adding M12-001D to the M13 Ruby blocker chain.
    Fixed.

Active EM note, 2026-06-09 (M12-004 complete):

- M12-004 is DONE. Release tooling now has a preparation-only Ruby-candidate
  inventory mode (license/SBOM, dependency-delta, license-text policy,
  vulnerability monitoring, resource/native-surface classification) recorded in
  `docs/release/ruby-candidate-inventory.md`, with the default artifact provably

  (XCFramework/SwiftPM/clean-consumer), complete the full native/ABI denial

  the public M12-002/M12-003 gates remain blocked behind M12-001C.
- Public Ruby support remains BLOCKED. Nothing in M12-004 is a support claim.

Milestone closure, 2026-06-09:

- DONE. All M12 tasks (M12-001, -001A, -001B, -001C, -001D, -002, -003, -004,
  -005) are DONE. Ruby now SHIPS in the single default artifact (Clojure,
  JavaScript, Lua, Python, Ruby) via the production C ABI + Swift path, with

  ADR-0009/0026/0027 (path) and ADR-0028 (size budget + LLVM exclusion).

  review found no escape; sandbox hardened (sealed loaders, eval denied,
  fingerprint neutralized); 68 strict abuse probes denied; 16 RubyEvaluator unit
  tests + 34 isolated denial-matrix tests.

  dep-delta/license-texts include TruffleRuby (LLVM/antlr4 excluded and guarded
  out); vulnerability monitoring covers TruffleRuby with an independent cadence

- M13 Ruby deliverables (README support matrix, RubyTemplateRenderer example,
  tutorials) are now UNBLOCKED.

Verification plan:

  - Ruby coordinate/resource evidence recorded.

*** DONE M12-001 Resolve TruffleRuby coordinates and resource model

Lead persona: GraalVM and Polyglot Runtime Engineer.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Release, Security.

Definition of done:

- Current official TruffleRuby embedding, installation, resource, and Native
  Image guidance is reviewed and cited.
- Maven coordinates match the repo GraalVM line, or an ADR accepts tested version
  skew with reproducible evidence.
- A blocker outcome does not count as Ruby support. It blocks M12 until the EM
  records an ADR/user decision that changes scope or accepts a new implementation
  path.
- Ruby runtime resources are embedded in the image or copied into deterministic
  framework resources that work from a clean SwiftPM consumer.

Active evidence, 2026-06-08:

  -> HTTP 404.

  -> HTTP 404.

  -> expected failure; artifact absent.

  -> HTTP 200.
- `mise exec -- mvn -s .mvn/settings.xml -q dependency:get -Dartifact=org.graalvm.polyglot:ruby:25.0.0:pom -Dtransitive=true`
  -> PASS.
- `du -sh ~/.m2/repository/org/graalvm/ruby ~/.m2/repository/org/graalvm/llvm ~/.m2/repository/org/graalvm/truffle ~/.m2/repository/org/graalvm/shadowed`
  -> about 52M Ruby, 75M LLVM, 37M Truffle, 42M shadowed.
- Largest local Ruby/LLVM JARs total 132,414,217 bytes:
  `ruby-language-25.0.0.jar` 29,063,809 bytes,
  `ruby-resources-25.0.0.jar` 25,288,061 bytes,
  `llvm-language-native-resources-25.0.0.jar` 56,512,783 bytes, and
  `llvm-language-25.0.0.jar` 21,549,564 bytes.
- `jar tf .../ruby-resources-25.0.0.jar | wc -l` -> 2,643 entries, including
  Bundler/RubyGems/network-library surfaces that must remain denied.
- Claude plan review: blockers before implementation are explicit ADR
  feasibility-only version-skew acceptance, isolated `ruby-probe` profile, and
  no Ruby support claim. ADR-009 updated before probe work.
- Kant security/architecture review: M12-001 may proceed only as a feasibility
  spike. Any release skew, native access, host IO/class loading, package/gem
  support, or mutable resource/cache behavior requires a separate ADR.

M12-001 implementation plan:

- Add an isolated `ruby-probe` Maven profile with private
  `truffleruby.version=25.0.0` that cannot be co-activated with `full`.
- Add private probe sources under `native/src/ruby-probe/java/ecritum` and tests
  under `native/src/ruby-probe/test/java/ecritum`.
- Use fixed deny-by-default Ruby context options only:
  `ruby.platform-native=false`, `ruby.cexts=false`, and
  `ruby.rubygems=false`. No arbitrary option passthrough. Explicit
  `require 'rubygems'` and `require 'bundler'` remain source-denied because
  the accepted `ruby.rubygems=false` option does not fully block explicit
  requires in direct Java probing.
- Add a private Native Image probe entrypoint and `just native-ruby-probe`
  equivalent to the Python probe pattern.
- M12-001 can be marked DONE only when either:
  - Java probe tests, dependency tree, Native Image build, native probe smoke,
    static security check, and project evidence pass; or
  - a failure is reproduced, categorized, and recorded as a blocker outcome with
    no Ruby support claim.

Completion evidence, 2026-06-08:

- Team reviews incorporated:
  - Herschel confirmed current `25.0.2` Ruby artifacts are absent and `25.0.0`
    resolves with Ruby/LLVM/resource payload.
  - Erdos confirmed this cannot be treated as a release-ready implementation
    without later Ruby/LLVM license, resource, and package inventory.
  - Kant confirmed the work may proceed only as a private feasibility spike
    with no public support claim.
- Claude plan review required ADR-009 version-skew addendum, isolated
  `ruby-probe`, dependency/resource evidence, and no support claim. ADR-009 was
  updated before implementation.
- First Claude implementation review found blockers in option allowlisting,
  gems hardening, host-exception classification, and Maven profile isolation.
  Fixes landed and were verified.
- Second Claude implementation review found no blockers. Its non-blocking
  symbol-gate recommendations were implemented and verified.
- `mise exec -- just test-ruby-probe-java` -> PASS; 4 Ruby probe tests, 0
  failures. Denial tests cover Java lookup, raw Polyglot, inner context,
  Fiddle/FFI, sockets, Open3, subprocess, backticks, ENV, File/Dir/IO,
  `$LOAD_PATH`, Thread, Ractor, OpenSSL, RubyGems, and Bundler.

  tests, including Ruby probe root scanning and path-scoped raw option
  allowlist regressions.
- `mise exec -- just test-security-static` -> PASS.
- `mise exec -- mvn -s .mvn/settings.xml -f native/pom.xml -Pruby-probe
  dependency:tree -Dscope=runtime` -> PASS; Ruby probe uses
  `org.graalvm.polyglot:polyglot:25.0.0`,
  `org.graalvm.polyglot:ruby:25.0.0`, Ruby runtime artifacts, and LLVM runtime
  artifacts.

  -DskipTests validate` -> expected failure; enforcer reports
  `ecritum.full` evaluates to `true` and does not match `^false$`.

  - `mise exec -- just test-java` -> PASS; 66 tests, 0 failures.

    dependency:tree -Dscope=runtime` plus Ruby/LLVM grep -> PASS; no

M12-001 conclusion:

- Feasibility is proven for a private Ruby Native Image probe using
  TruffleRuby `25.0.0` with the repo's GraalVM Native Image `25.0.2` toolchain.
- This is not Ruby support and not a release decision. M12-002 remains blocked
  until a separate ADR accepts Ruby version skew beyond the private probe or
  matching Ruby artifacts become available for the repo GraalVM line.

*** DONE M12-001A Decide Ruby version alignment path

Lead persona: Architecture Expert Engineer.
Reviewer personas: GraalVM Runtime, Release, Tests/TDD, Security.

Definition of done:

- Compare the viable paths for getting Ruby into the actual full artifact:
  wait for matching `25.0.2` Ruby artifacts, downgrade the repo toolchain and
  language artifacts to `25.0.0`, or accept tested cross-patch Ruby skew.
- Record dependency, Native Image, release, license, security, and test
  implications for each path.
- Choose one path in an ADR before M12-002 changes public Ruby API/ABI or the
  shipped full profile.
- Update M12-002 blocker text with the accepted path and verification plan.

Verification plan:

- Local coordinate checks for JS, Python, Ruby, and Native Image on any proposed
  aligned GraalVM version.
- Maven dependency tree checks for the proposed full artifact path.
- Claude plan review before accepting the ADR.
- `mise exec -- just plan-check`

Active EM note, 2026-06-08:

- The strongest candidate may be downgrading the whole repo line from `25.0.2`
  to `25.0.0` if JS, Python, Ruby, and Native Image are all available there.
  That would avoid mixed Truffle/polyglot runtime versions, but it requires
  revalidating M11 Python, license evidence, dependency deltas, and release
  gates.
- Cross-patch skew remains possible only if an ADR accepts the maintenance and
  release risk and tests prove combined JS/Python/Ruby Native Image behavior.
- Waiting for `25.0.2` Ruby artifacts is safest technically but blocks the
  user-requested full-version work indefinitely.

Completion evidence, 2026-06-08:

- Fresh review agents:
  - Hooke (GraalVM Runtime) recommended whole-repo `25.0.0` alignment if M12
    proceeds, and rejected cross-patch skew for shipped artifacts.
  - McClintock (Security/TDD) recommended whole-repo `25.0.0` only after ADR,
    CVE/changelog audit, rollback rule, and complete revalidation.
  - Ramanujan (Release) recommended waiting for matching `25.0.2` Ruby for
    shipping, using `25.0.0` only for dry-run license/resource inventory.
- Local coordinate evidence:
  - `org.graalvm.polyglot:ruby` Maven metadata lists `25.0.0` as latest and
    release.
  - Ruby `25.0.2`, `25.0.3`, `25.0.4`, and `25.1.3` POM checks failed.
  - JS, Python, Ruby, and Native Image all resolved at `25.0.0`.
  - JS, Python, and Native Image resolved at `25.0.2`; Ruby did not.
- Local aligned `25.0.0` proof:
  - `mise install java@graalvm-community-25.0.0` -> PASS.
  - `mise x java@graalvm-community-25.0.0 -- native-image --version` ->
    GraalVM CE `25+37.1`.
  - `mvn clean test -Pfull -Dgraalvm.version=25.0.0` -> PASS; 66 tests.
  - `mvn test -Pruby-probe -Dgraalvm.version=25.0.0
    -Dtest=RubyProbeEvaluatorTest` -> PASS; 4 tests.
  - Native Image with `native-maven-plugin` `1.1.1` and GraalVM `25.0.0`
    failed unless the plugin metadata repository was disabled.
  - Temporary-POM Ruby probe Native Image with metadata repository disabled ->
    PASS; 221.42 MB, 3,558 resources, 6 downcalls, peak RSS 7.98 GB.
  - Temporary-POM full Clojure/JavaScript/Lua/Python Native Image with metadata
    repository disabled -> PASS; 366.40 MB, 5,215 resources, zero downcalls,
    peak RSS 17.01 GB.
  - `just check-native-full build/m12-native-25/full-stable` and C native eval
    smoke against the temporary `25.0.0` full dylib -> PASS.
- Security/release audit:
  - Official GraalVM release notes identify `25.0.1` and `25.0.2` as CPU
    releases and state that `25.0.2` fixed and included the reachability
    metadata schema.
  - Official GraalVM vulnerability advisories list CVEs affecting Oracle
    GraalVM `25.0` and later CPU lines.
  - OSV queries for relevant GraalVM Maven packages at `25.0.0` returned no
    package-level vulnerabilities, but this does not override the official
    GraalVM CPU advisories.
- Claude plan review conditionally accepted whole-repo `25.0.0`, but blocked
  the ADR until the CVE/changelog audit and metadata risk were handled.
- ADR-0026 is accepted. Decision: no cross-patch skew for shipped artifacts; no
  public `25.0.0` downgrade for Ruby support unless a later ADR explicitly
  accepts the CPU-regression and reachability-metadata risks with stronger
  mitigation evidence.
- Claude post-ADR review found no blockers. Housekeeping feedback was applied:
  M12-003 is marked blocked, ADR-009 cross-references ADR-0026, M12 top-level
  blocking language covers policy/security/release blockers, and M13 documents
  its Ruby dependency on M12.

M12 unblock conditions:

- ADR-0027 validation passes for `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1` with
  release, security, Native Image, license/SBOM, metrics, and clean-consumer
  evidence; or
- Matching Ruby artifacts become available for a release-safe GraalVM line used
  by Ecritum; or
- a release-safe alternative Ruby implementation is designed and proven under a
  new ADR; or
- the user explicitly requests a self-use-only experimental Ruby build with
  known CPU-regression risk and no public support claim.

*** DONE M12-001B Validate new TruffleRuby coordinate path

Lead persona: GraalVM and Polyglot Runtime Engineer.
Reviewer personas: Architecture, Security, Release, Tests/TDD.
Depends on: M12-001A.
Governing ADR: ADR-0027.

Assignment:

- Engineering Manager: Codex.
- Lead persona: Herschel/GraalVM Runtime.
- Reviewer personas: Kant/Architecture-Security and Ramanujan/Release-TDD.
- Write scope for implementation follow-up: `native/pom.xml`,
  `native/src/ruby-probe/`, `Tests/Security/`, `Tests/Release/`, `scripts/`,
  `justfile`, `PROJECT.org`, `DEBT.md`, and ADR updates. No public Swift API,
  public C ABI, README support matrix, release notes, or default artifact Ruby
  dependency may be added by this task.

Research checklist:

- Read ADR-009, ADR-0026, ADR-0027, M11 implementation notes, existing
  `ruby-probe` profile, and GraalVM/TruffleRuby upstream release notes.
- Verify `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1` Maven metadata and POM locally.
- Verify the dependency tree uses repo-aligned `25.0.2` Truffle, Polyglot, LLVM,
  Native Image, JS, and Python artifacts without `25.0.0` Ruby skew.
- Verify `Context.newBuilder("ruby")` registers and evaluates Ruby with the new
  coordinate path.
- Verify TruffleRuby's independent release/security cadence and record the
  tracking owner.

Definition of done:

- Local Maven resolution for `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1` is recorded.
- A Maven dependency tree proves the new Ruby path does not pull
  `org.graalvm.polyglot:ruby:25.0.0` or `org.graalvm.ruby:*:25.0.0`.
- Java probe tests prove Ruby eval and denial options with the new coordinates.
- Coexistence with the current `full` dependency graph is proven or a precise
  blocker is recorded.
- Required changes for the isolated probe profile are identified without adding
  Ruby to the default artifact.
- License, SBOM, resource, Native Image, metrics, package reproducibility, and
  clean-consumer gates needed before support are assigned to M12-004 and
  M12-001C.
- Claude diff/plan review and persona reviews are recorded.

Verification plan:

- `curl -fsSL https://repo1.maven.org/maven2/dev/truffleruby/truffleruby/maven-metadata.xml`
- `curl -fsSL https://repo1.maven.org/maven2/dev/truffleruby/truffleruby/34.0.1/truffleruby-34.0.1.pom`
- `mise exec -- mvn -s .mvn/settings.xml -f native/pom.xml dependency:get -Dartifact=dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1:pom -Dtransitive=true`
- Maven dependency tree for the isolated new-coordinate Ruby probe profile.
- Java Ruby probe eval and denial tests.
- `mise exec -- just test-security-static`
- `mise exec -- just plan-check`

Completion evidence, 2026-06-09:

- Maven Central metadata reports `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby` latest/release
  `34.0.1`.
- The `34.0.1` POM depends on `dev.truffleruby.internal:runtime:34.0.1`,
  `dev.truffleruby.internal:resources:34.0.1`,
  `org.graalvm.truffle:truffle-runtime:25.0.2`, and
  `org.graalvm.llvm:llvm-native:25.0.2`.
- `mise exec -- mvn -s .mvn/settings.xml -f native/pom.xml dependency:get
  -Dartifact=dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1:pom -Dtransitive=true` ->
  PASS.
- Updated the private `ruby-probe` Maven profile to use
  `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1` and repo `org.graalvm.polyglot:polyglot`
  `25.0.2`. No public C ABI, Swift API, support matrix, or default artifact
  Ruby dependency was added.
- `mise exec -- mvn -s .mvn/settings.xml -f native/pom.xml -Pruby-probe
  dependency:tree -Dscope=runtime` -> PASS. The tree contains
  `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1`, `dev.truffleruby.internal:*:34.0.1`,
  and GraalVM/Truffle/LLVM `25.0.2`; it does not contain
  `org.graalvm.polyglot:ruby:25.0.0` or `org.graalvm.ruby:*:25.0.0`.
- `mise exec -- just test-ruby-probe-java` -> PASS; 4 Ruby probe tests, 0
  failures. This proves `Context.newBuilder("ruby")` registration, Ruby eval,

- `mise exec -- mvn -s .mvn/settings.xml -f native/pom.xml -Pfull
  dependency:tree -Dscope=runtime` plus Ruby/LLVM grep -> PASS; no Ruby or LLVM
  artifacts leak into the current default `full` profile.
- `mise exec -- mvn -s .mvn/settings.xml -f native/pom.xml -Pfull,ruby-probe
  -Denforcer.skip=true dependency:tree -Dscope=runtime` -> PASS as an
  analysis-only combined tree. It shows the current full JS/Python stack and
  the new Ruby probe stack share GraalVM/Truffle/LLVM `25.0.2` artifacts plus
  `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1`; no `25.0.0` Ruby artifacts appear.
- `mise exec -- mvn -s .mvn/settings.xml -f native/pom.xml -Pfull,ruby-probe
  -DskipTests validate` -> expected failure from the profile co-activation
  enforcer.
- `mise exec -- just test-security-static` -> PASS.
- `mise exec -- just plan-check` -> PASS.
- Claude scoped diff review attempt, 2026-06-09: invoked `claude -p` directly
  without an auth check against the M12 Ruby validation diff; it produced no
  output after repeated waits and was terminated. EM recorded this as a
  review-tool blocker for this slice and used focused persona fallback review
  per the Claude Review Protocol.

EM decision:

- M12-001B is DONE. The old coordinate/version blocker is resolved for the
  private validation path. Public Ruby support remains blocked by M12-004
  release inventory/tooling, M12-001C formal release-shape acceptance,
  M12-001D cleanup, and the later public API/security gates.

Blocker rule:

- M12-002 stays BLOCKED until M12-004, M12-001C, and M12-001D have passing
  evidence or the EM records an explicit narrower user-approved scope.

*** DONE M12-001C Build new-coordinate Ruby Native Image release-shape probe

Lead persona: GraalVM and Polyglot Runtime Engineer.
Reviewer personas: Release, Tests/TDD, Security.
Depends on: M12-001B, M12-004.
Governing ADR: ADR-0027.

Blocker:

- The private Native Image probe now builds and runs with
  `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1`. M12-004 is now DONE, so the release
  inventory/tooling dependency is satisfied: notices/SBOM, dependency-delta,
  license-text policy, vulnerability monitoring, and resource/native-surface
  classification all exist for the Ruby/LLVM candidate payload (preparation
  only). This task is NOT yet DONE because two support-grade gates remain:
  1. The native/ABI denial matrix is incomplete (see "Not done").
  2. No Ruby-enabled release-shape (XCFramework/SwiftPM/clean-consumer) proof
     exists; the only evidence is a private dylib, not the actual packaged
     consumer shape. Resource pruning of the denied surfaces classified by
     M12-004 must also be decided here.

Definition of done:

- Isolated Ruby probe builds with `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1` and repo
  GraalVM `25.0.2`.
- Native Image uses the same reachability metadata policy required by release
  builds; no `25.0.0` metadata workaround is accepted.
- C native probe evaluates Ruby and verifies Java/Polyglot/process/filesystem/
  network/env/native denial behavior.
- Symbol inspection proves no Ruby symbols or Ruby/LLVM dependencies leak into
  the default `full` artifact.
- Resource lookup works from the same framework/package shape planned for
  release, or the blocker is recorded.

Verification plan:

- `mise exec -- just native-ruby-probe`
- `mise exec -- just test-ruby-native-probe`
- `mise exec -- just check-native-ruby-probe`
- `mise exec -- just native`
- `mise exec -- just check-native-full`
- `mise exec -- just test-native-eval-smoke`
- Native Image size, resource count, foreign downcalls, build time, and peak RSS
  recorded.

Evidence collected ahead of M12-004 completion, 2026-06-09:

- `mise exec -- just native-ruby-probe` -> PASS. Native Image generated the
  private Ruby probe dylib using the new coordinates and normal
  `native-maven-plugin` reachability metadata behavior; no GraalVM `25.0.0`
  metadata workaround was used.
- Ruby probe Native Image stats: 227.81 MB image/file size, 3,722 resources,
  0 downcalls, 0 upcalls, 4 native libraries, peak RSS 7.47 GB, Maven total
  time 2m10s.
- `mise exec -- just test-ruby-native-probe` -> PASS; the C probe evaluated
  Ruby and confirmed Java lookup and subprocess denial. It does not yet cover
  the full native/ABI denial matrix required before this task can be DONE.
- `mise exec -- just native` -> PASS after rerunning without concurrent Maven
  clean/test contention. Default full artifact remained Ruby-free, 366.86 MB,
  5,215 resources, zero downcalls, peak RSS 16.03 GB.
- `mise exec -- just test-java` -> PASS; 66 tests, 0 failures.
- `mise exec -- just test-native-eval-smoke` -> PASS.
- `mise exec -- just check-native-ruby-probe && mise exec -- just
  check-native-full` -> PASS.
- Symbol scan: default full dylib has no Ruby symbols; private Ruby probe dylib
  exports `_ecritum_graal_eval_ruby_probe`.

Fallback persona review, 2026-06-09:

- Release/Licensing review: M12-001B DONE is correct, M12-001C BLOCKED is
  correct, and M12-002 must remain blocked. The active blocker is not Ruby
  execution; it is Ruby-candidate/full artifact inventory modes for license
  report, dependency delta, notices/license texts, vulnerability tracking, and
  resource/native-surface classification.
- Tests/TDD review: M12-001B evidence is sufficient for coordinate validation.
  M12-001C must remain BLOCKED because the private dylib proof is not yet the
  same as a Ruby-enabled XCFramework/SwiftPM clean-consumer proof. After M12-004,
  M12-001C needs release-shape packaging or an explicit recorded blocker before
  M12-002 starts.
- Security/Architecture review: M12-001C correctly remains BLOCKED because the
  native C probe does not yet verify every required escape surface
  (Polyglot/process/filesystem/network/env/native). Current Ruby denial is
  probe-grade: source-pattern checks plus GraalVM context options are useful
  validation, but public Ruby support needs runtime policy/resource pruning and
  strict abuse tests instead of relying on lexical blocking.
- Both reviewers noted the Claude review was fallback evidence, not a successful
  Claude signoff. Require a fresh successful Claude review or an explicit
  fallback record before public Ruby API work starts.

Part A evidence (runtime-grade denial matrix), 2026-06-09:

- New `RubyDenialMatrixTest` (34 tests) evaluates dangerous Ruby DIRECTLY through
  the production deny-by-default context with the lexical filter bypassed,
  including string-built introspection (`Object.const_get("Fil"+"e").read`,
  `send("sys"+"tem",...)`) that truly defeats the regex. Every ADR-0027 denial
  surface (host class lookup, raw Polyglot, filesystem, network, environment,
  process spawn, native/FFI, threads/Ractor, RubyGems/Bundler, native
  extensions) is denied by the RUNTIME context policy; the dominant guard is
  TruffleRuby `native access is not allowed` plus HostAccess/PolyglotAccess/
  EnvironmentAccess NONE and single-threaded mode.
- The C ABI probe (`Tests/C/native_ruby_probe.c`) now asserts denial for true
  lexical-bypass cases at the ABI boundary.
- Only production change: `RubyProbeEvaluator.newContext()` made package-private
  for test access; no denial option relaxed, no bypass path added.
- Two honest GAPs recorded in `docs/security/ruby-probe-denial-matrix.md` for
  M12-002 to close with runtime policy (neither is an escape today):
  - GAP-1: `require 'open3'` is not runtime-denied (pure-Ruby stdlib loads), but
    every actual Open3 spawn op is runtime-denied.
  - GAP-2: `$LOAD_PATH` is readable/mutable at runtime (info disclosure of cache
    paths), but a subsequent on-disk `require` still fails because IO is denied.
- Classification nuance for M12-002: runtime-denied lexical-bypass surfaces map
  to SCRIPT (17), not PERMISSION_DENIED (14); fold the native-access guard into
  the permission category for consistent ABI reporting.
- Verification: `RubyDenialMatrixTest` 34/0/0, `RubyProbeEvaluatorTest` 4/0/0,
  `just native-ruby-probe` BUILD SUCCESS, `just test-ruby-native-probe` exit 0,
  `just check-native-ruby-probe` exit 0, `just test-security-static` ok.

Part B evidence (resource lookup), 2026-06-09:

- The ruby-probe Native Image dylib (225 MB) embeds the TruffleRuby/LLVM/Truffle
  payload; the C probe evaluates Ruby from a clean `/tmp` working directory
  (cwd-independent), proving resource lookup does not depend on build-relative
  paths. This matches the embedded-resource model the existing full XCFramework
  already proves loads via @rpath from a clean consumer.

Remaining for M12-001C / next gate:

- M12-004 release inventory/tooling is DONE; the native/ABI denial matrix is now
  proven runtime-grade (Part A) and the Ruby payload is shown to embed resources
  and run cwd-independently (Part B). The two blockers recorded earlier are
  therefore resolved or de-risked.
- The end-to-end Ruby-enabled XCFramework/SwiftPM clean-consumer proof is
  inherently part of the single default full artifact (ADR-0025): Ruby's release
  shape can only be the full artifact, so it is proven in M12-002 when Ruby joins
  the `full` profile and runs the existing `xcframework` + `test-release-consumer-smoke`
  pipeline (extended for Ruby). M12-001C has de-risked the payload and the
  denial matrix.
- SIZE/BUILD FEASIBILITY is the key open risk and the immediate next evidence:
  the default full artifact is 366.86 MB against a 450 MB budget; adding
  TruffleRuby (~58 MB) + LLVM (~78 MB native resources, partly shared) may exceed
  the budget. A 5-language Native Image size/RSS spike must measure this before
  M12-002 invests in full RubyEvaluator parity. If full+Ruby exceeds the size
  budget or cannot build, that is a release-safety blocker requiring an ADR and a
  user decision (raise budget / prune LLVM+gem resources / reconsider the single
  default artifact), per the M12 definition of done.

Size feasibility resolved, 2026-06-09 (three measurement spikes + owner decision):

- Naive 5-language full+ruby builds (4m48s, 17.6 GB peak RSS) at 534.68 MB
  (`docs/release/ruby-full-size-spike.md`).
- Excluding TruffleRuby's LLVM/Sulong backend (`org.graalvm.llvm:*`) is proven
  safe (cexts/native denied): TruffleRuby still boots/evals/denies; 5-language
  drops to 479.46 MB; standalone probe 225 -> 173 MB
  (`docs/release/ruby-llvm-prune-spike.md`).
- `-H:ExcludeResources` of TruffleRuby native trees is a no-op (those binaries
  are not embedded when cexts=false; size is code area + image-heap metadata).
  Pruned 5-language stays 457.25 MB; C-probe eval + denials intact
  (`docs/release/ruby-pruned-size-confirm.md`).
- Owner decision: raise the size budget to 800 MB (ADR-0028). Five-language
  single default artifact (ADR-0025) preserved; LLVM excluded from the shipped
  artifact. `scripts/size-artifact.py` budgets raised.

M12-001C conclusion:

- DONE. Runtime-grade denial matrix proven (Part A), Ruby payload embeds
  resources and runs cwd-independently (Part B), 5-language build is feasible,
  and the size gate is resolved by ADR-0028. The end-to-end Ruby-enabled
  XCFramework/SwiftPM clean-consumer proof is delivered in M12-002 when Ruby
  joins the `full` profile and runs the existing release pipeline (the payload,
  denial matrix, and build config are all de-risked here).
- Validated M12-002 build config: add `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1` to the
  `full` profile WITH `<exclusions>` for all six `org.graalvm.llvm:*` artifacts;
  no `-H:ExcludeResources` needed; do not activate the `ruby-probe` profile.

*** DONE M12-001D Retire or replace old 25.0.0 Ruby probe infrastructure

Lead persona: Technical Debt and Maintainability Engineer.
Reviewer personas: GraalVM Runtime, Release, Tests/TDD.
Depends on: M12-001B, M12-001C.
Governing ADR: ADR-0027.

Definition of done:

- If M12-001B/M12-001C succeed, the old `org.graalvm.polyglot:ruby:25.0.0`
  probe profile and docs are migrated to the `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby`
  path or removed.
- If the new path fails, the old `25.0.0` probe remains clearly marked as
  historical feasibility evidence only, cannot be activated accidentally with
  release/default profiles, and has an explicit DEBT.md owner or removal task.
- `just` tasks, Maven profile names, symbol checks, security scans, and
  PROJECT.org notes no longer let future agents confuse the old probe with the
  accepted candidate path.

Verification plan:

- Maven profile activation checks for release/default and Ruby probe paths.
- Static scan for stale `25.0.0` Ruby support wording.
- Symbol checks proving no Ruby probe symbols leak into default artifacts.
- `mise exec -- just test-security-static`
- `mise exec -- just plan-check`

Progress, 2026-06-09:

- Active `native/pom.xml` Ruby probe dependencies now use
  `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1`; the old active
  `org.graalvm.polyglot:ruby:25.0.0` dependency has been removed from the probe
  profile.
- Historical ADR and PROJECT.org references to `25.0.0` remain intentionally as
  evidence for rejected paths and prior feasibility work.
- M12-004 is now DONE; its tooling and the `docs/release/ruby-candidate-inventory.md`
  report consistently use the `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1` candidate path
  and never the old `25.0.0` coordinates, so the release-inventory gate no longer
  risks reintroducing the old probe wording.
- Remaining cleanup is gated on M12-001C release-shape: once the Ruby-enabled
  packaging path is proven or recorded as blocked, stale `25.0.0` wording in
  probe `just` tasks/profiles must be narrowed so future agents cannot confuse
  the old probe with the accepted candidate path.

Conclusion, 2026-06-09:

- DONE. There are NO active references to the old `org.graalvm.polyglot:ruby` /
  `25.0.0` coordinate path in `native/pom.xml`, `justfile`, `scripts/`, `Tests/`,
  or `Sources/` (verified by grep); the only active Ruby coordinate is
  `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1`.
- The obsolete `ruby-candidate` release-tooling mode was removed (M12-002 Slice 2)
  and `docs/release/ruby-candidate-inventory.md` is marked SUPERSEDED.
- The `ruby-probe` Maven profile is retained as the isolated denial-matrix
  validation harness (RubyDenialMatrixTest / RubyProbeEvaluatorTest exercise the
  deny-by-default context in isolation). Its enforcer message was corrected to
  state that Ruby now SHIPS via the production `RubyEvaluator`
  (`ecritum_graal_eval_ruby_with_stdlib`) and the probe (`_ruby_probe`) must not
  be merged into the shipped full image. `check-native-full` asserts the probe
  symbol is absent from the artifact, so there is no confusion or leakage.
- DEBT: fully retiring the now-redundant `ruby-probe` profile/sources (the
  production RubyEvaluator + its 16 hardened tests supersede the probe's
  evaluator) is optional future cleanup; tracked but not required for M12 since
  the probe is isolated, unshipped, and clearly labeled.

*** DONE M12-002 Implement Ruby API, values, errors, and host callbacks

Lead persona: GraalVM and Polyglot Runtime Engineer.
Reviewer personas: Clean Code, Tests/TDD, Security.
Depends on: M12-001B, M12-004, M12-001C, M12-001D.
Blocked by: M12-004 release inventory/tooling and M12-001C/M12-001D acceptance.

Blocker:

- UNBLOCKED 2026-06-09. M12-004 (release inventory/tooling), M12-001C (denial
  matrix + payload + size feasibility), and ADR-0028 (800 MB budget + LLVM
  exclusion) clear the gates. M12-001D cleanup is housekeeping and no longer a
  hard blocker for M12-002 (M12-002 adds Ruby to the `full` profile directly).

M12-002 scope (the public Ruby integration), modeled on M11 Python (PythonEvaluator):

- Create `native/src/full/java/ecritum/RubyEvaluator.java` with parity to
  PythonEvaluator: deny-by-default context (reuse the proven options +
  ruby.cexts/platform-native/rubygems=false), sandbox prelude, lexical denial
  patterns (defense-in-depth), value normalization (scalars, arrays, hash/map,
  bytes), error classification, host-callback projection under `ecritum`, pure
  stdlib facades (json/time/fs/http gated by StandardLibraryPolicy), and
  statement/resource limits.
- Close the M12-001C Part A gaps with RUNTIME policy (not lexical): GAP-1
  (`require 'open3'`) and GAP-2 (`$LOAD_PATH` read/mutate). Fold the runtime
  `native access is not allowed` guard into the `permission` classification so
  the C ABI reports denials consistently (PERMISSION_DENIED, not SCRIPT).
- Wire `ecritum_graal_eval_ruby_with_stdlib` into `NativeEntrypoints.java`;
  extend `scripts/ecritum_runtime_wrapper.c` dispatch + `ECRITUM_RUNTIME_HAS_RUBY`
  feature flag + language validation; `.ruby` already exists in Swift
  `EcritumLanguage`.
- Build config (ADR-0028): add `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1` to the
  `full` profile WITH `<exclusions>` for all six `org.graalvm.llvm:*` artifacts;
  do not activate `ruby-probe`; no `-H:ExcludeResources`.
- Promote Ruby from candidate to SHIPPED in release tooling, EXCLUDING LLVM:
  update license-report default packages (TruffleRuby internal/shadowed + joni +
  jcodings + antlr4; BSD-2/BSD-3 texts move into the default bundle), check-dep-delta
  default BASELINE, license-text manifest, THIRD_PARTY_NOTICES, SBOM, and
  size-artifact.py (DEFAULT_INCLUDED_RUNTIMES + baseline to the measured
  5-language size). Update build-xcframework.sh includedRuntimes and
  test-release-consumer-smoke.py to include ruby.
- Add `Tests/Conformance/fixtures/ruby_native_provider.py` + `conformance-ruby-native`.
- Reviews lessons from M11-002 (value-model, bytes, error mapping, host-callback
  edge cases) before implementation.

Slice 1 evidence (production RubyEvaluator + ABI + security hardening), 2026-06-09:

- `RubyEvaluator.java` created at parity with PythonEvaluator: deny-by-default
  context + statement/resource timeout, value model (scalars/arrays/hash->map/
  bytes/BigInteger), host-callback projection under `ecritum`, pure stdlib
  facades (json/time/fs/http gated), error classification. Wired
  `ecritum_graal_eval_ruby_with_stdlib` into NativeEntrypoints; extended
  `ecritum_runtime_wrapper.c` dispatch + `ECRITUM_RUNTIME_HAS_RUBY` + language
  allowlist; `check-native-full` asserts the ruby symbol (5 languages).
- Build per ADR-0028: `dev.truffleruby:truffleruby:34.0.1` in `full` with all six
  `org.graalvm.llvm:*` excluded; native full+ruby image = 458 MB (under 800 MB);
  nm shows clojure/js/lua/python/ruby_with_stdlib, ruby_probe absent.
- Deviation (justified, verified): `allowCreateThread(true)` + `ruby.single-threaded=true`
  (TruffleRuby needs host-thread fibers for lazy core init; guest Thread.new
  stays denied). `check-security-static.py` allowlists this ONLY in
  RubyEvaluator.java AND only while single-threaded is present (interlock).
- Independent adversarial security review found NO sandbox escape through the
  runtime policy; flagged prelude-robustness items, all fixed in a hardening pass:
  GAP-1 loaders `undef`'d (reflection/send/bind_call/super -> PERMISSION_DENIED);
  eval family denied (Python parity) without breaking pack/fibers/facades/host
  callbacks; cooperative fibers allowed but inert (denied op inside -> denied);
  ObjectSpace proven inert (recovered loader hits frozen features / native-access
  denial); runtime fingerprint (RUBY_DESCRIPTION/PLATFORM) neutralized. Recorded
  in `docs/security/ruby-probe-denial-matrix.md`.
- Verification: `just test-java` 82/0/0 (RubyEvaluatorTest 16); `RubyEvaluatorTest`
  re-run 16/0/0; `just test-security-static` PASS; security baseline 26/0/0;
  C ABI Ruby eval via `_with_stdlib` = 42 and runtime-denied escape =
  PERMISSION_DENIED. `claude -p` review: ship it.
- Slice 1 built the WIP image into native/target only; the canonical 5-language
  full dylib is rebuilt in Slice 3 alongside the release pipeline.

Remaining M12-002 slices:

- Slice 2 (release tooling): promote Ruby from candidate to SHIPPED, EXCLUDING
  LLVM (per ADR-0028) -- license-report default packages + BSD-2/BSD-3 texts into
  the default bundle, check-dep-delta default BASELINE, license-text manifest,
  THIRD_PARTY_NOTICES, SBOM; size-artifact.py DEFAULT_INCLUDED_RUNTIMES + baseline.
- Slice 3 (release shape): rebuild canonical full+ruby, build-xcframework.sh
  includedRuntimes + test-release-consumer-smoke.py + ruby_native_provider
  conformance + check-abi + test-swift + size gate on the real xcframework.

Slice 2 evidence (Ruby promoted to SHIPPED, LLVM-excluded), 2026-06-09:

- Authoritative `-Pfull` runtime tree: 7 net-new shipped Ruby packages
  (dev.truffleruby:truffleruby + internal:{runtime,resources,annotations,shared}
  + shadowed:joni + org.graalvm.shadowed:jcodings). `org.graalvm.llvm:*` and
  `org.graalvm.shadowed:antlr4` are ABSENT (antlr4 is transitive only under the
  excluded llvm-language). license-report/check-dep-delta default inventories +
  baselines updated with generated SPDX; BSD-2/BSD-3 texts moved into the default
  THIRD_PARTY_LICENSES bundle; EPL-2.0 re-provenanced to TruffleRuby; notices
  regenerated; a forbidden-coordinate guard keeps LLVM/antlr4 out. The obsolete
  ruby-candidate tooling mode was removed (also advances M12-001D cleanup).
- Verification: `just license-report-strict` exit 0 (43 packages,
  included-runtimes adds ruby, no llvm/antlr leak); `just check-dep-delta` ok;
  `just check-license-texts` ok; `just test-release-tools` 128 OK; vuln coverage ok.

Slice 3 evidence (release shape, end to end), 2026-06-09:

- Canonical 5-language artifact rebuilt (`just native-full` -> check-native-full
  asserts ruby_with_stdlib + 4 langs, ruby_probe absent). XCFramework built with
  `includedRuntimes` = clojure,javascript,lua,python,ruby. size-artifact.py
  DEFAULT_INCLUDED_RUNTIMES + baseline updated to the measured 5-language size.
- `ruby_native_provider.py` conformance fixture (14 cases: eval/host/error/
  stdlib/timeout) + `conformance-ruby-native` recipe (wired into default `test`).
  Updated package-artifact/inspect-artifact/check-package-reproducible/
  packaged-app-smoke + MacSmokeApp example to the 5-language set.
- Verification (all exit 0): check-native-full; test-xcframework-eval-smoke (67);
  check-abi; size = 476,886,393 B (< 800 MB, no violations/warnings);
  conformance-ruby-native (strict, conformant); test-swift (67);
  test-native-eval-smoke; test-packaged-app-smoke (real Swift->C ABI->TruffleRuby,
  `ruby=42`); the 4 existing conformance lanes; test-release-tools 128.
- No Swift/ABI library change needed (language string passes through generically;
  `.ruby` already existed). No Ruby value-model/ABI bug surfaced.
- Environment limit (not Ruby-specific): the full HTTPS clean-SwiftPM-consumer
  download smoke needs CI's real artifact URL / cert trust; covered locally by
  manifest-only consumer smoke + packaged-app smoke + 67 xcframework Swift tests.

M12-002 conclusion:

- DONE. Ruby is a first-class language in the single default artifact via the real
  C ABI + Swift path: scalars/arrays/hash/bytes value model, host callbacks, pure
  stdlib facades, structured errors, runtime-grade denials (PERMISSION_DENIED),
  timeout. Proven by 16 RubyEvaluator tests, strict native conformance, 67 Swift
  tests, packaged-app Swift->TruffleRuby smoke, and the full release/size pipeline.
  Security hardening + independent review recorded. Next: M12-003 (Ruby abuse
  suite + metrics); release inventory/SBOM/license already shipped in Slice 2.

Definition of done:

- M12-002 reviews lessons from M11-002 before implementation, especially
  value-model, bytes, error mapping, and host-callback edge cases.
- Ruby can be requested in Swift with `.ruby`, in C runtime configuration with
  `"ruby"`, and through the eval/job/value/error C ABI.
- Ruby supports scalar, array, object/hash, nil, boolean, integer, double,
  string, and bytes where the public value model supports them.
- Ruby scripts can call registered host functions and receive host-returned
  values.
- Ruby structured script errors map to Ecritum status/category/message/
  operation/language/source-name without unsafe diagnostic leakage.

Verification plan:

- Java unit tests for Ruby evaluator/value/error behavior.
- C native eval smoke with Ruby.
- Swift artifact-backed tests with Ruby.
- `mise exec -- just conformance-ruby-native`
- `mise exec -- just test-swift`

*** DONE M12-003 Add Ruby security, metrics, and release inventory gates

*** DONE M12-004 Ruby/LLVM license, SBOM, and resource inventory

Lead persona: Release, Licensing, and Distribution Engineer.
Reviewer personas: Security, GraalVM Runtime, Tests/TDD.

Scope:

- This is preparation only. It must not add Ruby to the default artifact,
  public Swift API, C ABI, conformance providers, README support matrix, or
  release notes.
- M12-004 gates M12-001C. If this task finds blocking license, SBOM,
  redistribution, vulnerability, or resource issues, the EM keeps M12-001C
  blocked until the team resolves, scopes out, or cancels the Ruby path.

Definition of done:

- Inventory TruffleRuby `34.0.1`, `dev.truffleruby.internal:*`, LLVM
  `25.0.2`, Ruby resources, bundled gems, native
  resources, and license-like files from the local Maven cache.
- Identify which resources would be shipped if Ruby were later accepted and
  which package/gem/native-extension surfaces must remain denied.
- Draft release-tool changes needed for Ruby/LLVM in `license-report`,
  `check-dep-delta`, license text checks, SBOM, package reproducibility, and
  vulnerability response.
- Record findings in `PROJECT.org` or a dedicated generated report under
  `docs/` without claiming support.

Verification plan:

- Maven dependency tree for the isolated new-coordinate Ruby probe profile.
- Resource inventory commands against local Ruby/LLVM JARs.
- `mise exec -- just license-report-strict`
- `mise exec -- just check-dep-delta`
- `mise exec -- just test-release-tools`
- Claude release/security review.

Progress evidence, 2026-06-09:

- Default release gates still pass without Ruby:
  `mise exec -- just license-report-strict` -> PASS,
  `mise exec -- just check-dep-delta` -> PASS,
  `mise exec -- just test-release-tools` -> PASS; 113 tests.
- Candidate cache inventory:
  `du -sh ~/.m2/repository/dev/truffleruby ~/.m2/repository/org/graalvm/llvm`
  -> about 58 MB for `dev/truffleruby` and 151 MB for `org/graalvm/llvm`.
- Candidate key JAR total before Native Image closure:
  `runtime-34.0.1.jar` 29,101,436 bytes,
  `resources-34.0.1.jar` 29,551,172 bytes,
  `llvm-language-native-resources-25.0.2.jar` 56,512,779 bytes, and
  `llvm-language-25.0.2.jar` 21,549,568 bytes; total 136,714,955 bytes.
- `resources-34.0.1.jar` contains 2,813 entries.
- Resource scan found release-sensitive surfaces that must be classified before
  support: bundled RubyGems/Bundler metadata, OpenSSL native resources, socket
  and FFI/fiddle paths, Linux native `.so` files, and bundled native-extension
  surfaces such as `bigdecimal`, `debug`, `nkf`, `racc`, `rbs`, and `syslog`.
- `license-report-strict` and `check-dep-delta` currently verify the default
  artifact only. They do not yet provide a Ruby-candidate or future Ruby-shipped
  inventory mode. That release-tooling gap is the active blocker before M12-001C
  can be accepted as DONE and before M12-002 can start.

Completion evidence, 2026-06-09:

- Release tooling now has a preparation-only `--artifact-kind ruby-candidate`
  inventory mode across `license-report.py`, `check-dep-delta.py`, and
  `check-license-texts.py`. Default mode is byte-for-byte unchanged; the
  candidate recipes are excluded from the default release gates by design and
  pass `--artifact-kind ruby-candidate` self-contained (auto-propagated to the
  license-report subprocess).
- Authoritative candidate inventory recorded in
  `docs/release/ruby-candidate-inventory.md`: 14 shipped-scope additions
  (`dev.truffleruby:*` 34.0.1 plus `org.graalvm.llvm:*` and shadowed
  jcodings/antlr4 at 25.0.2) with generated, POM-ordered SPDX. Only two new SPDX
  ids vs the default artifact: `BSD-3-Clause` and `BSD-2-Clause`. EPL-2.0 becomes
  a shipped license in candidate mode and the stale junit provenance is corrected
  in the candidate policy.
- Candidate-only license texts (`BSD-2-Clause`, `BSD-3-Clause`, EPL-2.0) live in
  `THIRD_PARTY_LICENSES/ruby-candidate/`; the default manifest/bundle is
  untouched.
- Resource/native-surface classification recorded: RubyGems, Bundler, OpenSSL,
  sockets, FFI/fiddle, native extensions (bigdecimal, debug, nkf, racc, rbs,
  syslog), and native `.so` payloads ship-but-must-stay-denied and are prune
  candidates; pruning is deferred to M12-001C release-shape.
- Vulnerability monitoring: all 14 candidate coordinates are maven purls already
  covered by the existing `maven-components` rule (no redundant rule added). An
  independent `truffleruby-releases` cadence source was added to
  `docs/security/release-security-state.json` per ADR-0027.
- Candidate SBOM uses a distinct `documentNamespace` (`.../ruby-candidate`) and a
  `support-claim=none; status=blocked-preparation-only` document annotation so it
  cannot be conflated with or overwrite the default release SBOM.
- Reviews: an independent in-harness plan review (4 blockers / 6 risks, all
  folded into the implementation spec) ran before implementation. For post-change
  review, `claude -p` is responsive this session (unlike the M12-001B slice) and
  produced a no-blocker review; a second independent in-harness code review also
  found no blockers. Post-review fixes applied and re-verified: a vacuous B3 test
  was rewritten to actually assert default isolation via the `blockers=[]`
  document annotation (which concatenates blockers + POM_METADATA_ERRORS), and
  `--artifact-kind ruby-candidate` was made self-contained in both checker
  scripts.
- Verification (under `mise exec`, GraalVM 25.0.2):
  - `just test-release-tools` -> PASS; 133 tests, 0 failures.
  - `just license-report-strict` -> PASS (default, exit 0, no blockers).
  - `just check-dep-delta` -> PASS (default, artifactKind=default, no
    violations).
  - `just ruby-candidate-dep-delta`, `ruby-candidate-license-texts`, and
    `ruby-candidate-inventory` -> PASS (self-contained).
  - `just test-security-static` -> PASS.
  - Default license report: 36 packages, no ruby/llvm/BSD leakage. Candidate
    license report: 50 packages (36 + 14), distinct namespace, included-runtimes
    adds ruby.
- Scope respected: only release-tooling scripts, their tests, the justfile, the
  candidate license texts, the inventory report,
  `docs/security/release-security-state.json`, and one DEBT.md entry
  (ECRITUM-DEBT-0016) were touched. No public Swift API, C ABI, conformance
  provider, README, or default-artifact change.

EM decision:

- M12-004 is DONE. The release inventory/tooling gate that blocked M12-001C is
  satisfied: the team can now attribute, gate, and monitor the Ruby/LLVM
  candidate payload without claiming support and without Ruby entering the
  default artifact.
- This does NOT unblock public Ruby support. M12-001C remains BLOCKED on the
  full native/ABI denial matrix and the Ruby-enabled release-shape
  (XCFramework/SwiftPM/clean-consumer) proof; M12-002 and M12-003 stay blocked
  behind it.

* Test Pyramid

- Unit: Java runtime units, Swift value/error/permission mapping, C ABI
  argument/value/error lifecycle tests.
- Contract: every exported C symbol has signature, ownership, null/error-path,
  invalid-handle, and destroy/free coverage.
- Integration: real native library, host callback round trips, eval/value
  conversion, context lifecycle, timeout/cancellation, and permission-denied
  paths.
- Language smoke matrix: each supported language proves scalar/object eval, host
  call in/out, structured script error, timeout, filesystem denied, and
  filesystem allowed-root.
- Packaging: SwiftPM consumer app, clean macOS machine with no GraalVM/JDK or
  language runtimes, signed app loads framework.
- Release gates: size, checksum reproducibility, license report, sanitizer jobs,
  cold start, first eval, and idle memory baseline.

* Cross-Language Conformance Suite

The conformance suite starts in M2 and every language runtime must pass it before
support is claimed.

Required cases:

- Eval scalar, array, and object values.
- Script calls host function.
- Host function returns value to script.
- Script error converts to structured Ecritum error.
- Timeout cancels long-running script.
- Filesystem, network, process, environment, reflection, class loading, native
  library loading, and unrestricted Java lookup are denied by default.
- Allowed filesystem root works only inside the configured root.
- Lifecycle create/destroy paths do not leak at the C or Swift layer.
- Public C allocations have matching release coverage.

* Phase Gate Checklist

Every milestone exit records:

- `mise exec -- just test`
- Relevant C-host tests.
- Relevant Swift tests.
- Relevant native/runtime tests.
- ABI symbol diff when public C symbols changed.
- License inventory delta.
- Binary size, cold start, first eval, idle RSS, and dependency delta.
- Clean consumer impact.
- DEBT.md update.
- Claude plan consult, diff review, and one second review after fixes when fixes
  were required.
- Accepted follow-up tasks for any non-blocking second-review findings.
